3.08.(1).sec=	Part 3.06(a) of the Company Disclosure Schedule contains a complete and correct list as of the date of this Agreement of all U.S., state and foreign:  (i) Patents owned by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, (ii) Registered Trademarks owned by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, and (iii) Registered Copyrights and material unregistered Copyrights owned by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.

3.08.(2).sec=	The Company and its Subsidiaries collectively own all right, title and interest in, or have the valid right to use, all of the Company IP, free and clear of all Encumbrances other than Permitted Liens, and there are no obligations or covenants to, or restrictions from any other Persons affecting the use, enforcement, transfer or licensing of the Owned Company IP by the Company and its Subsidiaries.

3.08.(3).sec=	The Company and its Subsidiaries are the sole and exclusive beneficial owners, and, with respect to applications and registrations, record owners, of all the Owned Company IP.

3.08.(4).sec=	The Owned Company IP and Licensed Company IP constitute all the Intellectual Property necessary to conduct the businesses of the Company and its Subsidiaries as currently conducted.

3.08.(5).sec=	The Owned Company IP and, to the Knowledge of the Company, Licensed Company IP, are valid, subsisting and enforceable.

3.08.(6).sec=	No Owned Company IP or Licensed Company IP is being licensed, enforced or otherwise used in a manner that would result in the abandonment, cancellation or unenforceability of such Intellectual Property.

3.08.(7).sec=	Use by the Company and its Subsidiaries of any Company IP, and the conduct of their respective businesses, does not infringe, misappropriate, or otherwise violate any rights of any person, and no proceeding is pending or, to the Knowledge of the Company, has been threatened or asserted against the Company or any of its Subsidiaries with regard to the ownership, use, infringement, misappropriation, violation, validity or enforceability of any Company IP.

3.08.(8).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has infringed, misappropriated or otherwise violated any Intellectual Property of any Third Party.

3.08.(9).sec=	To the Knowledge of the Company, no Person is infringing, misappropriating, or otherwise violating any rights of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries in or to any Company IP.  No Proceeding is pending or has been threatened or asserted by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries against any person with regard to the ownership, use, infringement, misappropriation, violation, validity or enforceability of any Company IP.

3.08.(10).sec=	The Company and its Subsidiaries have taken reasonable actions to protect the confidentiality of their Trade Secrets and other confidential information.

3.08.(11).sec=	The consummation of the Contemplated Transactions, and compliance by the Company with the provisions of this Agreement, will not result in the termination, cancellation, loss, or impairment of, nor require the payment of additional amounts or the consent of any Person in respect of, or result in the creation of any Encumbrance in or upon, any Company IP.

3.08.(12).sec=	Section 3.08(l) of the Company Disclosure Schedule contains each Privacy Policy in effect at any time and identifies, with respect to each Privacy Policy, (i) the period of time during which such privacy policy was or has been in effect, (ii) whether the terms of a later Privacy Policy apply to the data or information collected under such privacy policy, and (iii) if applicable, the mechanism (such as opt-in, opt-out, or notice only) used to apply a later Privacy Policy to data or information previously collected under such privacy policy.  Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries either has or had any electronic or other database containing (in whole or in part) Personal Data or User Data.  The Company and each of its Subsidiaries have complied at all times and in all material respects with all of the Privacy Policies and with all applicable Legal Requirements pertaining to privacy (including the obtaining, storing, using or transmitting of User Data), User Data or Personal Data.  Neither the execution, delivery, or performance of this Agreement (or any of the Ancillary Agreements) nor the consummation of any of the Contemplated Transactions, nor the Parent’s possession or use of User Data, will result in any violation of any Privacy Policy or any applicable Legal Requirement pertaining to privacy, User Data or Personal Data.

3.09.Ti=	Property; Sufficiency of Assets.  

The Company and its Subsidiaries (i) have good, valid and, in the case of real property, marketable title to, or valid leasehold or sublease interests or other comparable contract rights in or relating to, all of the real property and other tangible assets used in or necessary for the conduct of their business as currently conducted, including good and valid title to all real property and other tangible assets reflected in the latest audited financial statements included in the Company SEC Reports as being owned by the Company and its Subsidiaries or acquired after the date thereof (other than property sold or otherwise disposed of in the ordinary course of business since the date thereof), free and clear of all Encumbrances, except for 

(A)	Encumbrances for Taxes not yet due and payable or due but not delinquent or being contested in good faith and for which adequate reserves have been established, 

(B)	Encumbrances for assessments and other governmental charges or Encumbrances of landlords, carriers, warehousemen, mechanics and repairmen incurred in the ordinary course of business consistent with past practices, in each case for sums not yet due and payable or due but not delinquent or being contested in good faith and for which adequate reserves have been established, 

(C)	Encumbrances incurred in the ordinary course of business consistent with past practices in connection with workers’ compensation, unemployment insurance and other types of social security or to secure the performance of tenders, statutory obligations, surety and appeal bonds, bids, leases, government contracts, performance and return of money bonds and similar obligations and 

(D)	Encumbrances that do not materially interfere with the conduct of the Company’s business and do not materially affect the use or value of the Company’s assets  

(collectively, "Permitted Liens”), and (ii) are collectively the lessee of all property material to the business of the Company and its Subsidiaries which is purported to be leased by the Company and its Subsidiaries and are in possession of such properties, and each lease for such property is valid and in full force and effect without material default thereunder by the lessee or the lessor.  All material items of equipment and other tangible assets owned by or leased to the Company and its Subsidiaries are sufficient for the uses to which they are being put, are in good and safe condition and repair (ordinary wear and tear excepted) and are sufficient for the conduct of the business of the Company and its Subsidiaries in the manner in which such business is currently being conducted.  Part 3.09 of the Company Disclosure Schedule lists all material real property and any material interest in real property owned by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.

3.10.Ti=	Taxes.

3.10.(1).sec=	The Company and its Subsidiaries have filed or caused to be filed all Tax Returns that are or were required to be filed by or with respect to any of them, either separately or as a member of a group of corporations, pursuant to applicable Legal Requirements.  All Tax Returns filed by (or that include on a consolidated basis) the Company or any of its Subsidiaries were (and, as to Tax Returns not filed as of the date hereof, will be) in all material respects complete and correct and filed on a timely basis.

3.10.(2).sec=	The Company and its Subsidiaries have, within the time and in the manner prescribed by law, paid all Taxes that are due and payable by them.

3.10.(3).sec=	The Company and each of its Subsidiaries have complied in all material respects with all applicable Legal Requirements relating to the payment and withholding of Taxes (including withholding and reporting requirements under the Code or Code sections 1441 through 1464, 3401 through 3406, 6041 and 6049 and similar provisions under any other Legal Requirements ) and have, within the times and in the manner prescribed by applicable Legal Requirements , withheld from employee wages and paid over to proper Governmental Authorities all amounts required to be so withheld and paid.

3.10.(4).sec=	As of the date of this Agreement, neither the Company not any of its Subsidiaries has received any written or unwritten notice that any Tax Return of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is under audit or examination by any Taxing Authority and there are no matters under discussion with any Taxing Authority with respect to Taxes.  Part 3.10(d) of the Company Disclosure Schedule lists, and the Company has delivered to Parent copies of, all examiner’s or auditor’s reports, notices of proposed adjustments or similar commissions received by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries from any Taxing Authority since [•].  The United States income tax returns of the Company and its Subsidiaries consolidated in such returns have been examined by and settled with the Internal Revenue Service (the "IRS”) for all years, or all years are otherwise closed, through the taxable year ended [•].

3.10.(5).sec=	The charges, accruals, and reserves with respect to Taxes on the respective books of the Company and each of its Subsidiaries are adequate to pay all Taxes not yet due and payable and have been determined in accordance with GAAP.  No differences exist between the amounts of the book basis and the Tax basis of assets (net of liabilities) that are not accounted for on any accrual on the books of the Company and its Subsidiaries for federal income tax purposes.  There exists no proposed assessment of Taxes against the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.

3.10.(6).sec=	No Encumbrances for Taxes exist with respect to any assets or properties of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, except for statutory liens for Taxes not yet due.

3.10.(7).sec=	Part 3.10(g) of the Company Disclosure Schedule lists as of the date of this Agreement, and the Company has delivered to Parent copies of, any Tax sharing agreement, Tax allocation agreement, Tax indemnity obligation or similar written or unwritten agreement, arrangement, understanding or practice with respect to Taxes (including any advance pricing agreement, closing agreement or other agreement relating to Taxes with any Taxing Authority) to which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is a party or by which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is bound.

3.10.(8).sec=	As of the date of this Agreement, neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has requested any extension of time within which to file any Tax Return, which Tax Return has not since been filed.

3.10.(9).sec=	As of the date of this agreement, neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has executed any outstanding waivers or comparable consents regarding the application of the statute of limitations with respect to any Taxes or Tax Returns.

3.10.(10).sec=	No power of attorney currently in force has been granted by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries concerning any Taxes or Tax Return.

3.10.(11).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has received or been the subject of a Tax Ruling or a request for Tax Ruling.  Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has entered into a Closing Agreement with any Governmental Authority that would have a continuing effect after the Closing Date.  "Tax Ruling” means a written ruling of a Governmental Authority relating to Taxes.  "Closing Agreement” means a written and legally binding agreement with a Governmental Authority relating to Taxes.

3.10.(12).sec=	Part 3.10(l) of the Company Disclosure Schedule lists as of the date of this Agreement, and the Company has made available to Parent, complete and correct copies of all Tax Returns, and any amendments thereto, filed by or on behalf of, or which include, the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, for all taxable periods that have ended since [•].

3.10.(13).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries is required to include in income any adjustment pursuant to Section 481 of the Code by reason of a voluntary change in accounting method initiated by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, and the IRS has not proposed any such change in accounting method.

3.10.(14).sec=	No election under Section 338 of the Code has been made by or with respect to the Company or any of its Subsidiaries or any of their respective assets or properties.

3.10.(15).sec=	As of the date of this Agreement, neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has engaged in any transactions with Affiliates that would require the recognition of income by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries with respect to such transaction for any period ending on or after the Closing Date.

3.10.(16).sec=	The disallowance of a deduction under Section 162(m) of the Code for employee remuneration will not apply to any amount paid or payable by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries under any Company Contract, Company Benefit Plan, program, arrangement or understanding currently in effect.

3.10.(17).sec=	As of the date of this Agreement, neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries is a party to any agreement, contract or arrangement that would result separately or in the aggregate, in the payment of an "excess parachute payment” within the meaning of Section 280G of the Code in connection with the Contemplated Transactions.

3.10.(18).sec=	As of the date of this Agreement, no claim has ever been made by a Governmental Body in a jurisdiction where neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries files Tax Returns that the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is or may be subject to taxation by that jurisdiction.

3.10.(19).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries (A) has been a member of an "affiliated group” within the meaning of Code Section 1504(a) filing a consolidated federal income Tax Return (other than a group the common parent of which was the Company) or (B) has any liability for the Taxes of any Person (other than the Company and its Subsidiaries) under United Stated Treasury Regulations Section 1.1502-6 (or any similar provision of state, local, or foreign law), as a transferee or successor, by contract, or otherwise.

3.10.(20).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries will be required to include any item of income in, or exclude any item of deduction from, taxable income for any taxable period (or portion thereof) ending after the Closing Date as a result of any (x) installment sale or open transaction disposition made on or prior to the Closing Date, or (y) prepaid amount received on or prior to the Closing Date.

3.10.(21).sec=	Neither the Company nor any of its Subsidiaries has distributed stock of another Person, or has had its stock distributed by another Person, in a transaction that was purported or intended to be governed in whole or in part by Code Sections 355 or 361.

3.11.Ti=	Employee Benefits.  

3.11.(1).sec=	As used in this Agreement: "Controlled Group Liability” means any and all liabilities under (i) Title IV of ERISA, (ii) Section 302 of ERISA, (iii) Sections 412 and 4971 of the Code, (iv) the continuation coverage requirements of Section 601 et seq. of ERISA and Section 4980B of the Code, and (v) corresponding or similar provisions of foreign laws or regulations, other than such liabilities that arise solely out of, or relate solely to, the Company Benefit Plans; "ERISA” means the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974, as amended, and the regulations thereunder; "ERISA Affiliate” means, with respect to any entity, trade or business, any other entity, trade or business that is a member of a group described in Section 414(b), (c), (m) or (o) of the Code or Section 4001(b)(1) of ERISA that includes the first entity, trade or business, or that is a member of the same "controlled group” as the first entity, trade or business pursuant to Section 4001(a)(14) of ERISA.

3.11.(2).sec=	Except as required under this Agreement, since •, there has not been:

3.11.(2).(1).sec=	any adoption or material amendment by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries of any collective bargaining agreement or any bonus, pension, profit sharing, deferred compensation, incentive compensation, stock ownership, stock purchase, stock option, restricted stock, phantom stock, stock appreciation right, retirement, vacation, severance, disability, death benefit, hospitalization, medical, worker’s compensation or supplementary unemployment benefits plan or arrangement or any employment agreement with any employee, officer, director or independent contractor of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries who, as of the date of this Agreement, is among the ten most highly compensated of such individuals, in each case that provides compensation or benefits to any current or former employee, officer, director or independent contractor of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries or any beneficiary thereof or sponsored, entered into, maintained or contributed to, as the case may be, by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries or their ERISA Affiliates or with respect to which the Company and its Subsidiaries or their ERISA Affiliates otherwise have any liabilities or obligations (collectively, "Company Benefit Plans”), or

3.11.(2).(2).sec=	any adoption of, or amendment to, any Company Benefit Plans which would materially increase the expense of maintaining such Company Benefit Plans above the level of the expense incurred in respect thereof for the fiscal year ended on[•].

Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, the term "Company Benefit Plans” includes all employee welfare benefit plans within the meaning of Section 3(1) of ERISA, all employee pension benefit plans within the meaning of Section 3(2) of ERISA.  Except as expressly contemplated hereby, neither the execution and delivery of this Agreement nor the consummation of the Contemplated Transactions will (either alone or in conjunction with any other event) result in, cause the accelerated vesting or delivery of, or increase the amount or value of, any payment or benefit to any current or former employee, officer, director or independent contractor of the Company and its Subsidiaries.

COMMENT:

[NTD:  Commentary re benefits reps above not yet included.]

Rule 14d-10 "Best Price Rule” Representation.

[Sub-sections (t), (u) and (v) above address the seller’s compliance with the SEC’s "best price” rule.  

Exchange Act Rule 14d-10 includes the "best price rule,” which requires that consideration paid to each security holder tendering in a tender offer be the highest consideration paid to any other security holder for their tendered securities.  The consequences of a violation of the rule can be quite high; every stockholder potentially could claim the difference between what the stockholder received and what the favored stockholder received.  For example, if an executive received payment ostensibly as a closing bonus that was deemed under the rule to be consideration for his or her shares, then all stockholders potentially would have a claim to the same additional per-share consideration for all of their shares.  With that leverage, even a small payment in violation of the rule could lead to large damages, particularly if the recipient owned relatively few shares.  

A series of cases largely in the years 1995 through 2003 found violations of the rule arising from payments under compensation or severance arrangements triggered by the tender offer (see, e.g., Gerber v. Computer Assoc., 303 F.3d 126, 136 (2d Cir. 2002) (portion of confidentiality agreement payment to Chairman and CEO of target company determined to be payment for his tendered shares); Epstein v. MCA, Inc., 50 F.3d 644, 655 (9th Cir. 1995) (finding a Capital Contribution and Loan Agreement with the target company’s Chairman and CEO to violate Rule 14d-10)).  Given this uncertainly, and the potentially large damages, use of the tender offer became very limited, with parties opting to use a one-step merger, in which the best price rule does not apply (see Amendments to the Tender Offer Best-Price Rules, Exchange Act Release No. 54,684 (Dec. 8, 2006)).  

To reduce uncertainty around the best price rule, the SEC amended it in 2006 to clarify that the rule only applies to the consideration for securities tendered in the tender offer.  The amended rule:

•	specifies that the consideration subject to best price requirements is the "consideration paid to any security holder for securities tendered in the tender offer” rather than consideration paid to a security holder "pursuant to the tender offer,”

•	provides that the best price provisions do not prohibit negotiation, execution or amendment of compensatory arrangements, and

•	contains a non-exclusive safe harbor for certain compensatory arrangements approved as compensatory arrangements by the compensation committee of the target company or the bidder, as applicable.

The amended rule, including the certainty of the safe harbor has had the intended effect of reinstating the tender offer as a viable transaction structure in many instances, evidenced by an increase in the number of tender offers and by the absence of new court decisions finding violation of the best price rule.

Non-Compensatory Arrangements.

While the Instruction to paragraph (d) of Rule 14d-10 states that the express references to employment compensation, severance and other employee benefit arrangements as exclusions from best price restrictions do not preclude the ability to enter into commercial or other arrangements with tendering security holders under the best price rule, the absence of safe harbors for these other arrangements means that a bidder must assess the risk of argument that a commercial or other agreement completed in connection with a tender offer is actually a premium for securities tendered by the other party to the arrangement.  Additional risk also potentially arises from an argument that the arrangement effectively constitutes a purchase outside the tender offer, which is prohibited under Exchange Act Rule 14e-5.  Third party valuations for fairness or market price in connection with commercial or other arrangements involving a security holder may help mitigate these risks.  

Given the text of the amended rule, and its applicability to securities tendered, an agreement not to tender by a stockholder that is also party to a commercial or other arrangement being completed around the time of the tender offer may provide additional protection against a Rule 14d-10 challenge.

In the private equity context, this type of Non-Tender and Support Agreement has been utilized with management of the target that will be receiving rollover equity in the acquiror.  These management representatives enter into the agreement before the launch of the tender offer, refrain from tendering in the tender offer, commit to vote in support of the second-step merger if a vote is required, and receive their roll over equity as consideration in the merger.  

Compensatory Arrangements and Safe Harbor

The best price rule is not violated by employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangements where the amounts payable thereunder are: 

•	being paid for past services performed, future services to be performed, or future services to be refrained from performing, by the security holder*; and

•	not calculated based on the number of securities tendered or to be tendered* in the tender offer.  

Rule 14d-10(2) provides a non-exclusive safe harbor, under which the requirements noted above for not violating the best price rule will be deemed to have been met.  The safe harbor arises if an arrangement is approved as an employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangement solely by independent directors of the subject company (regardless of whether it is party to the arrangement) or, if the arrangement will be with the bidder, by independent directors of the bidder.  Under Rule 14d-10(d)(2), the body of independent directors to approve the compensation arrangements is typically the compensation committee, and the discussion below refers to the compensation committee, but the Rule should be consulted for additional detail.  

In the Agreement, a bidder will typically seek confirmation of the satisfaction of the safe harbor in a representation, a covenant, or both.  This Agreement contains both a representation and a covenant (see Section 6.10), although if the target is not prepared to give a representation at the time of signing (which could be the case of the compensation committee has not had the opportunity to review and approve compensation arrangements under Rule 14d-10), the target should negotiate for having a prospective covenant only.  

From a bidder perspective, whether the provision is contained in a representation, covenant, or both is likely to be less significant than ensuring that its closing conditions require that the Compensation Committee of the target has acted consistently with the Rule 14d-10 safe harbor prior to the closing of the tender offer.  For the bidder, this condition would need to apply with respect to all compensation arrangements that could be called into question in a tender offer, with no material adverse effect carveout or other limitation, particularly given that protection of the safe harbor would depend on strict compliance with the provisions of the rule.  The bidder may also want a right to terminate if the target cannot satisfy the Rule 14d-10 safe harbor.

A 14d-10 representation or covenant is likely to address the following:

Arrangements being Approved as Employment Compensation, Severance or other Employee Benefit Arrangement.  In making its representations and covenants, a target will want to limit the employment arrangements being covered, both to avoid the risk of any potential liability from inadvertently including arrangements not considered by the compensation committee and to establish a clear set of arrangements being presented to the compensation committee for approval.  If the description of the agreements being reviewed by the compensation committee were overly broad, as a corporate law matter there could be questions raised as to the validity of the compensation committee’s action under its due care obligations.  

Length of Lookback.  In the representation as drafted above, there is description of the arrangements being considered and a time frame limitation of the past 18 months.  An 18-month lookback may be broader than what is necessary to give comfort that arrangements were not related to the tender offer (or there could be contexts where it is too narrow), and the assessment of the appropriate time period would have to be made in the context of the specific facts and the history of target and management consideration of a tender offer or other change of control.  Although the target will want to limit the set of arrangements being approved, it is also of interest of all parties to be certain that all applicable arrangements are addressed to have safe harbor coverage.

Breadth of Arrangements Covered.  The representation above covers any employment agreement, severance agreement or change of control agreement and any Company Options or Restricted Stock awarded or accelerated  Some buyers may ask for more, noting that they want comfort over any payments being made to relevant securities holders.  See Comment above on Non-Compensatory Arrangements.  For example, a bidder may request that the representation also cover:

"Any other arrangement with any holder of Shares who was or is a director, officer or employee of the Company or any Company Subsidiary that may reasonably be considered to be conditional on, related to or otherwise an integral part of the Offer or Merger.”

The Company may object to such expansion on the grounds that ____________.  [NTD:  Need to fill this out.]

Arrangements with the Bidder.  The Rule 14d-10 safe harbor allows the target’s Compensation Committee to approve arrangements that tendering equity holders are making with parties other than the target, such as arrangements with the bidder.  The target may in this instance wish to push for the bidder’s compensation committee to approve arrangements with the bidder or its affiliates because the bidder will have better information about such arrangements and their intent.  If it is successful in having the bidder’s compensation committee act, the target may wish to obtain a representation from the bidder of its compliance with the Rule 14d-10 safe harbor.  If the target’s compensation committee is approving arrangements with other parties, the target will want to maintain rights to receive all information related to such an arrangement that it needs to determine its approval, and the target may want a representation as to the completeness and accuracy of such information.

Buyers may ask for additional coverage, such as:  ___________________

Director Independence.  A Board determination of the independence of the directors approving the arrangement satisfies the 14d-10 safe harbor independence requirements.  The requirements regarding director independence generally follow listing standards of the applicable exchange.  The representation above requires the determination of independence not only at the time of the Agreement’s signing and closing but also as of the periods in which the arrangements were entered, which would be important if parties were relying on previous compensation committee actions.

3.15.(3).(2).sec=	to the Knowledge of the Company, as of the date of this Agreement, no event has occurred, and no circumstance or condition exists, that (with or without notice or lapse of time) will or would reasonably be expected to, (A) result in a violation or breach, in any material respect, of any of the provisions of any Material Contract, (B) give any Person the right to declare a default or exercise any remedy under any Material Contract, (C) give any Person the right to receive or require a material rebate, chargeback, penalty or change in delivery schedule under any Material Contract, (D) give any Person the right to accelerate the maturity or performance of any Material Contract, (E) result in the disclosure, release or delivery of any Company Source Code, or (F) give any Person the right to cancel, terminate or modify in any material respect any Material Contract; and

3.23.Ti=	Opinion of Financial Advisor.  

The Company’s board of directors has received the opinion of [•]dated •, to the effect that, as of such date, and based on the assumptions, qualifications and limitations contained therein, the consideration to be received by the stockholders of the Company pursuant to the Offer and the Merger is fair to such stockholders from a financial point of view.  

[NTD:  Comment below is from Model Merger Agreement]

COMMENT:

Prior to recommending a merger agreement for stockholder action, a board of a Delaware corporation must determine that the merger agreement is advisable, fair to, and in the best interests of the corporation and its stockholders.  DGCL, Sec. 251(b).  The directors’ fiduciary duty of due care requires that the board act in an informed and deliberate manner in determining whether to approve or disapprove the merger agreement.  Indeed, the Delaware Supreme Court has indicated that a board cannot simply "abdicate” and turn the decision as to whether to merge over to the stockholders.  "[A] director may not abdicate that duty by leaving to the stockholders alone the decision to approve or disapprove the agreement.”  Smith v. Van Gorkom, 488 A.2d 858, 873 (Del. 1985).  

Part of the directors’ duty of care obligation is to make an informed business judgment as to the financial fairness of the consideration to be received by the corporation’s stockholders in the merger.  In Van Gorkom, the Delaware Supreme Court cited the failure of a board to have sought or received a fairness opinion in connection with its approval of a merger agreement as evidence that the board had breached its duty of care in approving the merger agreement.  While the court did not state that a board is required to obtain a fairness opinion in order to satisfy its duty of care in approving a merger agreement, since the Van Gorkom opinion, it has become standard practice for the board of directors of a public target corporation to receive an opinion from an investment banking firm or other valuation firm that the consideration being offered in the merger to the target stockholders is fair to such stockholders from a financial point of view.  

Under Section 141(e) of the DGCL, a board is "fully protected” from liability if it relies in good faith on an opinion of an outside valuation firm selected with reasonable care as to matters within the outside firm’s competence, i.e., the fairness of the merger consideration.  However, this reliance must be reasonable and is qualified by the duty of good faith (i.e., boards may not blindly rely on these experts and should be engaged in the review of the fairness presentation and question unreasonable assumptions or "red flags”).  Generally, though, the financial fairness of a proposed transaction is only one of the factors that a board should consider in deciding whether to proceed with the transaction.

The buyer also has an interest in ensuring that the target board follows a proper procedure in approving a merger, since the failure to do so could result in either the merger being enjoined by a court or monetary liability being imposed following a transaction and significant defense costs for which the buyer may ultimately be responsible.  Accordingly, most buyers will insist that the target board receive a fairness opinion and will require a representation to that effect.  They may also request the opportunity to review the opinion to make sure nothing unusual is noted that could put the approval of the transaction at risk or give rise to potential future liability.

As financial advisors utilize different language in their fairness opinions, the actual language of the representation should track the language of the fairness opinion actually received by the target. 

[NTD:  Address likely Buyer request to receive opinion, or even engagement letter, or additional reps re financial advisor’s consent or company’s right to disclose the opinion and analyses.]

No broker, finder, investment banker or other Person (other than •) is or may be entitled to any brokerage, finder’s or other fee or commission in connection with the Merger and the Contemplated Transactions based upon arrangements or authorizations made by or on behalf of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.  

3.25.Ti=	[Full Disclosure.  

3.25.(1).sec=	This Agreement (including the Company Disclosure Schedule) does not, and the certificate referred to in Section[•]will not, (i) contain any representation, warranty or information that is false or misleading with respect to any material fact, or (ii) omit to state any material fact necessary in order to make the representations, warranties and information contained and to be contained herein and therein (in the light of the circumstances under which such representations, warranties and information were or will be made or provided) not false or misleading.]

ARTICLE 4

REPRESENTATIONS AND WARRANTIES OF PARENT AND MERGER SUB

Parent and Purchaser represent and warrant to Company, except as set forth or incorporated by reference (a) in the part of the disclosure schedule delivered to Company on the date of this Agreement (the "Parent Disclosure Schedule”) corresponding to the numbered section of this Article IV that includes a particular representation or warranty, or (b) in any other part of the Parent Disclosure Schedule where it is reasonably apparent from the face of such disclosure or the context in which such disclosure is made that such disclosure should qualify a particular representation or warranty, as follows:

COMMENT:

See the introductory Comment to Article III of the Model Tender Offer Agreement for a general overview of the impact of representations in a public company merger agreement with a first step tender offer.

Because the target’s stockholders will only be receiving cash in the tender offer and the merger, and will not be receiving equity of the buyer, the target’s interest in the buyer’s representations will be focused on the buyer’s financial and legal ability to consummate the transaction, and with ensuring their compliance with relevant disclosure obligations and other applicable legal requirements.  Accordingly, the Model Tender Offer Agreement does not include representations regarding the buyer’s SEC reports, financial statements, contracts, undisclosed liabilities or other similar matters.

A general qualification of the representations to the buyer’s SEC reports has not been included in the Model Tender Offer Agreement.  The buyer may argue that it would be unfair for the agreement to be asymmetrical in this regard and propose either that the parallel qualification included for target’s representations be removed (and the buyer may already be arguing for such a change) or that the buyer should also have the benefit of such qualification.  The target may respond that buyer’s representations are relatively limited and focused on matters unrelated to the buyer’s operations, and that there should therefore be no issue with making such representations on an unqualified basis.

As with Comments to Article III of the Model Tender Offer Agreement, Comments in Article IV use the term "representation” by itself to refer to the combined concept of "representations and warranties.”

4.01.Ti=	Organization, Standing and Power.  

4.01.(1).sec=	Parent and Purchaser are corporations or other entities duly incorporated or otherwise formed, validly existing, and in good standing (where such concept is recognized under the laws of the jurisdiction in which it is incorporated or formed) under the laws of their respective jurisdictions of incorporation or organization, with all necessary Entity power and authority to conduct their respective businesses as now being conducted and to own, lease or otherwise hold their respective properties and assets.

COMMENT:

This representation mirrors the target’s representation in Section 3.01 of the Model Tender Offer Agreement, with the exception of the representation regarding jurisdictions where the applicable entities are qualified to do business is not included.  Such a representation is not of interest to the target here given its focused interest on Parent’s and Purchaser’s respective abilities to fund and close the Offer and the Merger.

4.01.(2).sec=	Purchaser is a direct, wholly owned subsidiary of Parent that was formed solely for the purpose of engaging in the Contemplated Transactions.  Since the date of its incorporation, Purchaser has not carried on any business or conducted any operations other than the execution of this Agreement, the performance of its obligations hereunder and matters ancillary thereto.

COMMENT:

This representation almost invariably reflects the facts and the buyer usually will raise no objection to its inclusion.  [Both the target and the buyer will desire to maximize the potential for Parent to own greater than 90% of the target’s common stock following the Offer and any exercise of the top-up option so that the second-step merger can be accomplished via short-form merger under Section 253 or Section 267 of the DGCL, and any dilution in the ownership of Purchaser by Parent will make it more difficult to achieve that goal.] [NTD:  ELABORATE ON DILUTION]  

In addition, the target and the buyer will want to avoid any potential claims by shareholders of the surviving corporation regarding the fairness of the merger consideration paid in the second step merger as a result of the surviving corporation’s succession to any assets held by Purchaser, and consequently it would be preferable for both parties that Purchaser have no assets.

4.01.(3).sec=	Parent has delivered to the Company copies of the Organizational Documents of Parent and Purchaser, as currently in effect.  Such Organizational Documents are in full force and effect, and neither Parent nor Purchaser is or has been in violation of any of the provisions thereof.

COMMENT:

Section 4.01 does not provide a corresponding representation to that found in Section 3.01(b) which requires the Company to list all Subsidiaries and make a representation regarding the delivery of the applicable Organizational Documents for each Subsidiary because the target’s shareholders will only be receiving cash in the tender offer and the merger and will not have any continuing interest in the business thereafter.

4.02.Ti=	Authority; No Conflict.  

4.02.(1).sec=	Each of Parent and Purchaser has all necessary Entity power and authority to execute and deliver this Agreement and to consummate the Contemplated Transactions.  [The execution and delivery by Parent and Purchaser of this Agreement and the consummation by Parent and Purchaser of the Contemplated Transactions have been duly authorized by all necessary corporate action on the part of Parent and Purchaser and no other corporate proceedings on the part of Parent or Purchaser are necessary to authorize the execution and delivery of this Agreement and consummation of the Contemplated Transactions.] [NTD:  SEE BELOW]  Parent and Purchaser have each duly executed and delivered this Agreement.  This Agreement constitutes the legal, valid and binding obligation of Parent and Purchaser, enforceable against Parent and Purchaser in accordance with its terms, except to the extent that such enforcement may be subject to applicable bankruptcy, insolvency, reorganization, moratorium or other similar Legal Requirement affecting the enforcement of creditors’ rights generally and to general equitable principles (whether considered in a proceeding whether in equity or at law).

COMMENT:

If Purchaser holds less than 90% of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock following the consummation of the Offer (including any subsequent offering period, if applicable) and the exercise of the top-up option, Section 251 of the DGCL will apply, which requires that each of the constituent corporations submit the executed merger agreement to its stockholders for adoption subsequent to execution of the agreement and adoption of a resolution by the corporation’s board of directors approving the agreement and declaring its advisability.  In order for the Model Tender Offer Agreement to be properly authorized and effected by Purchaser under Section 251 of the DGCL, five events must occur in the following order:  

(1)	Purchaser’s board of directors must adopt a resolution approving the agreement and declaring its advisability; 

(2)	officers of Purchaser must execute and acknowledge the agreement; 

(3)	the agreement must be submitted to Purchaser’s stockholders (i.e., Parent) for adoption; 

(4)	the agreement must be certified; and 

(5)	the agreement or the certificate of merger must be filed with the Secretary of State.

If, on the other hand, Purchaser holds 90% or more of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock following the consummation of the Offer (including any subsequent offering period, if applicable) and the exercise of the top-up option, Section 6.04 of the Model Tender Offer Agreement provides that the parties will effect a short-form merger under Section 253 or Section 267 of the DGCL as soon as practicable thereafter, which requires only that the parent entity in such merger (i.e., Purchaser) execute and file a certificate of its ownership and merger with the Secretary of State that sets forth a copy of the resolutions of its board of directors approving the merger and states that the merger has been approved by its shareholders.  Because the target will not be wholly-owned, the resolutions of the board of directors must include the terms and conditions of the Merger.  However, because it will not be known at the time the agreement is signed whether or not Purchaser will hold 90% or more of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock following the consummation of the Offer, and the representation provides that all necessary corporate action has been taken on the part of Parent and Purchaser as of signing, they will in any case need to proceed under items (1)-(4) of the preceding paragraph substantially concurrently with signing.

Purchaser Stockholder Approval.  As a practical matter, no meeting of Purchaser’s stockholders will be held to adopt the Model Tender Offer Agreement.  Instead Parent (as Purchaser’s sole stockholder) will execute a written consent adopting the Model Tender Offer Agreement.  A meeting of stockholders is not required to approve a merger agreement if the agreement is approved by written consent pursuant to Section 228 of the DGCL by a majority of the holders of the stock entitled to vote on the agreement.  If a written consent is used, the secretarial certification should state that stockholder approval was obtained pursuant to written consent and that the notice required by Section 228(c) of the DGCL, if any, has been given.

It is important to remember that the buyer may not approve a merger agreement under Delaware law prior to its execution by all the parties thereto.  Some merger agreements represent that "Parent has approved the Merger Tender Offer Agreement in its capacity as the sole stockholder of Purchaser.”  This formulation should be avoided as such approval cannot legally occur under Delaware law until the agreement has been executed.  [NTD:  Would it be permissible to include the following language:  "By executing and delivering this Agreement, Parent hereby approves…”?]  [NTD:  GIVEN THIS TIMING CONSTRAINT, SHOULD THE LANGUAGE IN THE REP BE REVISED?  DO WE NEED A COVENANT AS TO PARENT’S POST-SIGNING APPROVAL AS STOCKHOLDER OF PURCHASER?]



4.02.(2).sec=	Neither the execution and delivery of this Agreement, nor the consummation of any of the Contemplated Transactions, will, except as have not had and could not reasonably be expected to have a Parent Material Adverse Effect: 

(i)	contravene, conflict with, or result in a violation or breach of (A) the provisions of the Organizational Documents of Parent or any of its Subsidiaries; (B) any Legal Requirement or any Order to which Parent or any of its Subsidiaries is subject, assuming that all filings and notifications in accordance with the HSR Act, and the filing of the Certificate of Merger in accordance with the DGCL, have been made; or (C) the provisions of any material Contract or any material Governmental Authorization of Parent or any of its Subsidiaries; or 

(ii)	result in the creation of any Encumbrance (other than a Permitted Lien) upon or with respect to any of the assets of Parent or any of its Subsidiaries.

COMMENT:

This representation mirrors the target’s representation in Section 3.02(c) of the Model Tender Offer Agreement.  

The buyer may suggest that because of the target’s limited interests in the buyer’s operations and assets, the scope of the representation should be reduced to not extend to subsidiaries other than Purchaser, to unrelated laws and contracts and/or to liens upon the buyer’s assets.  The target may respond that the representation is limited only to those matters that could have Parent Material Adverse Effect, and therefore that the scope of the representation is limited in a manner consistent with the target’s interests in the transaction.

4.02.(3).sec=	The execution and delivery of this Agreement by Parent and Purchaser do not, and the performance of this Agreement and the consummation of the Contemplated Transactions by Parent and Purchaser will not, require any Consent of, or filing with or notification to, any Person, except:

(i)	for (A) applicable requirements, if any, of the Exchange Act, the Securities Act and Blue Sky Laws, (B) the pre-merger notification requirements of the HSR Act, (C) filing of a certificate of merger as required by the DGCL and (D) the non-United States competition, antitrust and investment laws set forth in Part 3.2(c) of the Parent Disclosure Schedule and 

(ii)	where failure to obtain such Consents, or to make such filings or notifications, individually or in the aggregate, have not had and could not reasonably be expected to have a Parent Material Adverse Effect.

Notwithstanding the foregoing, no representation is made by Parent or Purchaser with respect to information expressly identified by the Company as having been provided for such purpose.  Each of the Offer Documents will, at the time that such document is filed with the SEC, at any time it is amended or supplemented or at the time it is first published, sent or given to the Company’s stockholders, comply as to form in all material respects with the applicable provisions of the Exchange Act and the rules and regulations promulgated thereunder.

4.04.Ti=	Brokers.  

Neither Parent nor Purchaser, nor any of their respective officers, directors or employees has employed any broker or finder or incurred any liability for any brokerage fees, commissions or finder’s fees in connection with the Transactions except [_________], whose fees and expenses will be paid by Parent in accordance with Parent’s agreement with such firm.

COMMENT:

The target’s interest in obtaining this representation from the buyer is largely to ensure that there is no relationship between its own financial advisors and those employed by buyer, and therefore no conflict of interest.

4.05.Ti=	Absence of Litigation.  

There is no suit, action or proceeding pending or, to the knowledge of Parent, threatened against Parent or any claim, Subsidiary of Parent that, individually or in the aggregate, has had or could reasonably be expected to have a Parent Material Adverse Effect.  There is no Judgment outstanding against Parent or any Subsidiary of Parent or any of their respective assets that, individually or in the aggregate, has had or could reasonably be expected to have a Parent Material Adverse Effect.  Parent has not received any written notification of, and to the knowledge of Parent there is no, investigation by any Governmental Entity involving Parent or any Subsidiary of Parent or any of their respective assets that, individually or in the aggregate, has had or could reasonably be expected to have a Parent Material Adverse Effect.

4.06.Ti=	Ownership of Company Common Stock.  

None of Parent, Purchaser or any of their "affiliates” or "associates” is, or at any time during the last three (3) years has been, an "interested stockholder” (as such terms are defined in Section 203 of the DGCL) of the Company.  Prior to the date hereof, neither Parent nor Purchaser has taken, or authorized or permitted any Representatives of Parent or Purchaser to take, any action that would reasonably be expected to cause, Parent Purchaser or any of their "affiliates” or "associates” to be deemed an "interested stockholder” (as such term is defined in Section 203 of the DGCL) or otherwise render Section 251(h) of the DGCL inapplicable to the Merger.

COMMENT:

This representation confirms that no higher vote of the target’s stockholders will be required under Section 203 of the DGCL as a result of the buyer owning 15% or more of the target’s voting stock without prior board approval and supports a determination that buyer is not an "affiliate” of target within the meaning of the Rule 13E-3(a)(1) of the Exchange Act.  This representation also confirms that, at the time the target board approves the merger agreement, neither Parent nor Purchaser will be an "interested stockholder” of the target; a prerequisite to the applicability of Section 251(h).

Under Rule 13E-3, if the buyer is affiliated with the target, and the target’s capital stock is being cashed-out in the transaction and will therefore no longer be listed on any securities exchange or registered with the SEC, both the buyer and the target would be required to file and disseminate to the target’s stockholders a Transaction Statement on Schedule 13E-3 that requires substantially enhanced disclosures regarding the transactions, the background thereof and the interests of the various parties therein.  Schedule TO allows the buyer to combine the Schedule TO and Schedule 13E-3 into one filing.

[NTD:  Discuss how much detail to provide regarding 13E-3 transactions.]

4.07.Ti=	Financing.  

Parent and Purchaser have sufficient funds available to consummate the Offer and the Merger on the terms contemplated by this Agreement and, at the expiration of the Offer and the Effective Time, Parent and Purchaser will have available all of the funds necessary for the acquisition of all shares of the Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer and the Merger, as the case may be, to pay all fees and expenses in connection therewith, to make payments to holders of Company Options pursuant to Section 2.05 and to perform their respective obligations under this Agreement.

4.08.Ti=	Pre-Closing Funding.  

Parent has and will continue to have sufficient working capital to meet its pre-Closing obligations hereunder, including funds to pay any filing fees and the costs of applying for, and obtaining, all approvals from Governmental Bodies.

COMMENT:

Sections 4.07 and 4.08 require the buyer to represent that it will have sufficient cash available to fund each of the payments they will be required to make at each transaction stage, as well as all of their expenses.

Financing.  Should it be contemplated that the buyer will obtain equity and/or debt financing in connection with the transactions, the buyer will not be able to represent that it has such funds available currently, and the target will typically request that the buyer make representations regarding those financing arrangements, regardless of whether the agreement includes any direct financing conditionality or indirect financing conditionality through inclusion of a financing related reverse break-up fee.  The following is an example of a provision that could be proposed by the target:

"Parent has delivered to the Company true, complete and correct copies of:

(i) executed commitment letters (as the same may be amended pursuant to Section ____, the "Debt Financing Commitments”), pursuant to which the lenders parties thereto have agreed, subject to the terms and conditions thereof, to provide or cause to be provided the debt amounts set forth therein (the "Debt Financing”), and 

(ii) executed equity commitment letters (the "Equity Financing Commitments”, and together with the Debt Financing Commitments, the "Financing Commitments”), pursuant to which [●] and [●] have committed, subject to the terms and conditions thereof, to invest the amount set forth therein (the "Equity Financing,” and together with the Debt Financing, the "Financing”).

Each of the Equity Financing Commitments is in full force and effect and is a legal, valid and binding obligation of Parent and of the other parties thereto.  Except as permitted by Section _____, the Debt Financing Commitments are in full force and effect as of the date of this Agreement and are legal, valid and binding obligations of Parent and the other parties thereto.  

None of the Financing Commitments has been or will be amended or modified, and the respective commitments contained in the Financing Commitments have not been and will not be withdrawn or rescinded in any respect, except as permitted by this Agreement.  No event has occurred which, with or without notice, lapse of time or both, would constitute a default or breach on the part of Parent or Purchaser under any Financing Commitment, and neither Parent nor Purchaser has any reason to believe that it will be unable to satisfy on a timely basis any term or condition to the funding or investing, as applicable, of the full amount of the Financing needed to be satisfied by it in any of the Financing Commitments.  There are no conditions precedent or other contingencies related to the funding or investing, as applicable, of the full amount of the Financing other than as expressly set forth in or contemplated by the Financing Commitments and there are no contractual or other contingencies under any contract, agreement, commitment, side letter or other arrangement relating to the Financing Commitments which permit any lender or investor to reduce the amount of any Financing or, except as provided in the Debt Financing Commitments, that would adversely affect or delay the availability of any Financing.

Subject to the terms and conditions of the Financing Commitments, and subject to the terms and conditions of this Agreement, the net proceeds contemplated from the Financing, together with other financial resources of Parent and Purchaser, including cash on hand, will, in the aggregate, through the expiration of the Offer and at the Acceptance Time, Effective Time and the Closing, provide funds to Parent and Purchaser sufficient for the acquisition of all shares of the Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer and the Merger, as the case may be, to pay all fees and expenses in connection therewith, to make payments to holders of Company Options pursuant to Section 2.04 and to perform their respective obligations under this Agreement.”

In some cases, including most acquisitions sponsored by private equity funds, the Parent entity proposed by the buyer will itself be a shell company that is formed for purposes of the acquisition having a sole source of funding consisting of an equity commitment from the funded buyer entity, such as the applicable private equity fund.  The target may argue that the funded buyer entity should either directly be party to the agreement as the "Parent” or provide a guaranty of all obligations of the Parent and Purchaser under the agreement.  Alternatively, the target may insist that the target be an express third party beneficiary of the equity commitment letter, and that funding under the equity commitment letter unconditionally cover all potential obligations of Parent and Purchaser under the agreement, and not just payments to stockholders upon consummation of the transactions as will frequently be proposed by buyers.  In either case, the target’s position will be that it should be no worse off in a structure using a parent shell entity backed by a guaranty or equity commitment structure than it would be if the funded buyer entity was a direct party to the agreement.

If the buyer’s equity commitment set forth in the equity commitment letter is for less than the full amount of Parent’s potential obligations under the agreement, as will typically be the case, the amount of such equity commitment will serve as an effective cap on the buyer’s potential liability for breaches of the Model Tender Offer Agreement.  In cases where a limited guaranty is used rather than an equity commitment letter, the buyer will typically include a cap on its liability thereunder, which will be subject to negotiation between the buyer and the target.  If a reverse break-up fee structure is included in the agreement, the equity commitment letter and/or guaranty will include limitations on liability that are consistent therewith.

As noted [cross-reference to discussion of dual-track structure], Regulation U and Regulation X will place limits on the buyer’s ability to use Company Common Stock acquired in the Offer as collateral to obtain financing to make such purchases, and may drive the buyer and the target towards a dual-track tender offer/traditional stockholders meeting structure similar to that utilized in the Burger King and Gymboree transactions.

[ADD IN ANY 251(h)-RELATED FINANCING ISSUES?  FINANCING CONDITION?  EXTENSION OF EXPIRATION DATE?  ROLLOVER?]

4.09.Ti=	Solvency.  

After giving effect to the transactions contemplated by this Agreement, including the payment of the aggregate Offer Price and Merger Consideration, the payment of all other amounts required to be paid in connection with the consummation of the Contemplated Transactions and the payment of all related fees and expenses, each of Parent and the Surviving Corporation will be Solvent as of the Effective Time and immediately after the Contemplated Transactions.  For the purposes of this Agreement, the term "Solvent” means that, as of any date of determination and with respect to any Person:

4.09.(1).sec=	the sum of the debt (including contingent liabilities) of such Person and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole, does not exceed the present fair saleable value of the present assets of such Person and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole;

4.09.(2).sec=	the capital of such Person and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole, is not unreasonably small in relation to the business of such Person and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole; and

4.09.(3).sec=	such Person and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole, do not have or intend to incur debts including current obligations beyond their ability to pay such debt as they mature in the ordinary course of business;

provided, for the purposes hereof, the amount of any contingent liability at any time shall be computed as the amount that, in light of all of the facts and circumstances existing at such time, represents the amount that can reasonably be expected to become an actual  or matured liability (irrespective of whether such contingent liabilities meet the criteria for accrual under Statement of Financial Accounting Standard No. 5).

4.10.Ti=	Absence of Certain Agreements.  

Neither Parent nor any of its Affiliates has entered into any agreement, arrangement or understanding (in each case, whether oral or written), or authorized, committed or agreed to enter into any agreement, arrangement or understanding (in each case, whether oral or written), pursuant to which: 

(i)	any stockholder of the Company would be entitled to receive consideration of a different amount or nature than the Offer Price or pursuant to which any stockholder of the Company agrees to vote to adopt this Agreement or the Merger or agrees to vote against any Superior Proposal;

4.11.Ti=	Foreign Ownership.  

Neither Parent nor Purchaser nor any person who, directly or indirectly, owns five percent (5%) or more beneficial interest in Parent is a foreign person as defined by 31 C.F.R. §800.216 or 22 C.F.R. §120.16.

4.12.Ti=	Interest in Competitors.  

None of Parent or Purchaser or any of their respective Affiliates or any other Person included within the same "person” (as defined in the rules under the HSR Act) as Parent or Purchaser is engaged in or owns an equity interest in any entity or Person that derives a significant portion of its revenues from the Business.

4.13.Ti=	WARN Act.  

Parent and Purchaser are neither planning nor contemplating, and Parent and Purchaser have neither made nor taken, any decisions or actions concerning the employees of the Company after the Acceptance Time that would require the service of notice under the WARN Act or similar local laws.

4.14.Ti=	No Other Representations and Warranties.  

Each of Parent and Purchaser acknowledges and agrees that it (a) has had an opportunity to discuss the business of the Company and its Subsidiaries with the Company’s management, (b) has had reasonable access to (i) personnel, properties, premises and books and records of the Company and its Subsidiaries and (ii) the "virtual data room” maintained by the Company for purposes of the Contemplated Transactions, (c) has conducted its own independent investigation and analysis of the Company and its Subsidiaries, their respective businesses and Contemplated Transactions, and each of Parent and Purchaser acknowledges and agrees that it has not been induced by and has not relied upon any representation, warranty or statement, whether express or implied, made by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, or any of their respective affiliates, stockholders, controlling persons or Representatives that are not expressly set forth in this Agreement, whether or not such representations, warranties or statements were made in writing or orally.

Parent and Purchaser each acknowledge and agree that, except for the representations and warranties expressly set forth in this Agreement (x) the Company does not make, or has not made, any representation or warranty relating to itself or its business or otherwise in connection with the Contemplated Transactions and Parent and Purchaser are not relying on any representation or warranty except for those expressly set forth in this Agreement, (y) no person has been authorized by the Company to make any representation or warranty relating to itself or its business or otherwise in connection with the Merger, and if made, such representation or warranty must not be relied upon by Parent or Purchaser as having been authorized by such party and (z) any estimates, projections, predictions, data, financial information, memoranda, presentations or any other materials or information provided or addressed to Parent, Purchaser or any of their Representatives are not and shall not be deemed to be or include representations or warranties unless any such materials or information are the subject of any express representation or warranty set forth in Article IV.

5.01.(2).(1).sec=	(A) declare, set aside or pay any dividends on, or make any other distributions (whether in cash, stock or property) in respect of, any of its capital stock or other equity or voting interests, except for dividends by a direct or indirect wholly owned Subsidiary of the Company to its parent, (B) split, combine or reclassify any of its capital stock or other equity or voting interests, or issue or authorize the issuance of any other securities in respect of, in lieu of or in substitution for shares of its capital stock or other equity or voting interests, or (C) purchase, redeem or otherwise acquire any shares of capital stock or any other securities of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries or any options, warrants, calls or rights to acquire any such shares or other securities (including any Company Equity Awards or other Company Stock-Based Rights except (x) ) from holders of Company Stock Options in full or partial payment of the exercise price, (y) in connection with the withholding of Taxes payable by any holder of Company Equity Awards or other Company Stock-Based Rights or (z) pursuant to agreements to repurchase shares at their original purchase price or forfeiture conditions of such forfeiture conditions of such shares);

5.02.Ti=	No Solicitation.  

5.02.(1).sec=	The Company shall immediately cease and cause to be terminated any existing discussions with any Person that relate to any Acquisition Proposal.  During the Pre-Closing Period, the Company and its Subsidiaries shall not, and the Company shall direct each Representative of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries not to, (i) solicit or initiate the submission of any Acquisition Proposal or knowingly take any action that could reasonably be expected to lead to an Acquisition Proposal, (ii) furnish any non-public information regarding the Company or any of its Subsidiaries to any Person in connection with or in response to an Acquisition Proposal, or (iii) engage in discussions or negotiations with any Person with respect to any Acquisition Proposal,

provided, however, that prior to the Acceptance Time, notwithstanding anything in this Agreement, the Company may furnish nonpublic information regarding the Company and its Subsidiaries to, or enter into discussions or negotiations (including solicitation of revised Acquisition Proposals) with, any Person in response to an Acquisition Proposal that was not the result of a material breach of this Section 5.02 and that the Company Board concludes in good faith, after consultation with its outside legal counsel and financial advisors, is, or could reasonably be expected to lead to, a Superior Proposal and prior thereto the Company receives from such Person an executed confidentiality agreement containing customary limitations on the use and disclosure of all nonpublic information furnished to such Person by or on behalf of the Company.

The Company shall provide to Parent, in accordance with and pursuant to the terms of the Confidentiality Agreement, any material non-public information concerning the Company or any of its Subsidiaries that is provided to such other Person that was not previously provided to Parent, to the extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements.

5.02.(2).sec=	Except as provided in this Section 5.02, (i) the Company Board shall not withdraw or modify, in a manner materially adverse to Parent, the Company Board Recommendation (a "Change in Recommendation”), (ii) the Company shall not enter into any letter of intent, memorandum of understanding or agreement relating to or providing for the consummation of an Acquisition Transaction (other than a confidentiality agreement to the extent permitted by Section 5.02(a)), and (iii) the Company Board shall not adopt, approve or recommend any Acquisition Proposal. 

Notwithstanding the foregoing or anything to the contrary set forth in this Agreement, at any time prior to the Acceptance Time, the Company Board may effect a Change in Recommendation if:

5.02.(2).(1).sec=	the Company Board shall have determined in good faith (after consultation with its outside legal counsel) that the failure to effect a Change in Recommendation is reasonably likely to be inconsistent with its fiduciary obligations under applicable Legal Requirements;

5.02.(2).(2).sec=	the Company has notified the Parent in writing (the "Company Notice”) that it intends to effect a Change in Recommendation, describing in reasonable detail the reasons for such Change in Recommendation (it being understood that this notice itself shall not constitute a Change in Recommendation or a Triggering Event for purposes of this Agreement), which Company Notice will include, if the proposed Change in Recommendation is in response to a Superior Proposal, the identity of the Third Party making the Superior Proposal, or if the proposed Change in Recommendation is in response to an Intervening Event, a summary of the Intervening Event;

5.02.(2).(3).sec=	if requested by the Parent, the Company shall have made its Representatives available to discuss with the Parent’s Representatives any proposed modifications to the terms and conditions of this Agreement during the two (2) business day period following delivery by the Company to the Parent of the Company Notice so that such Superior Proposal ceases to constitute a Superior Proposal or, with respect to an Intervening Event, as would permit the Company Board to not make a Change in Recommendation; and

5.02.(2).(4).sec=	if the Parent shall have delivered to the Company a written, binding and irrevocable offer to alter the terms or conditions of this Agreement during such two (2) business day period, the Company Board shall have determined in good faith (after consultation with its outside legal counsel), after considering the terms of such offer by the Parent, that the failure to effect a Change in Recommendation is still reasonably likely to be inconsistent with its fiduciary obligations under applicable Legal Requirements. 

5.02.(3).sec=	The Company shall promptly (and in any event within two (2) business day) notify Parent of any Acquisition Proposal (including the identity of the Person submitting such Acquisition Proposal and the material terms thereof) that is submitted by any Person during the Pre-Closing Period subject to the terms of any confidentiality agreement and to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements.  The Company shall, promptly (and in any event within two (2) business day) notify Parent of any material modification to any such Acquisition Proposal that is submitted by any Person during the Pre-Closing Period subject to the terms of any confidentiality agreement and to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements.

5.02.(4).sec=	The Company will request each Person that has executed a confidentiality agreement within 12 months prior to the date of this Agreement, in connection with its consideration of a possible Acquisition Transaction, to return all confidential information heretofore furnished to such Person by or on behalf of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.

5.02.(5).sec=	Nothing contained in this Section 5.02 or elsewhere in this Agreement shall prohibit the Company Board from taking and disclosing to the Company’s stockholders a position contemplated by Rule 14e-2(a) or Item 1012(a) of Regulation M-A promulgated under the Exchange Act or complying with the provisions of Rule 14d-9 promulgated under the Exchange Act, including making any "stop, look and listen” communication to holders of shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to Rule 14d-9 under the Exchange Act, or from making any disclosure to the Company’s stockholders if, in the good faith judgment of the Company Board, after consultation with its outside counsel, failure to make such disclosure would be inconsistent with the Company Board’s fiduciary duties or applicable Legal Requirements; provided, however, that this Section 5.02(f) shall not be deemed to permit the Company Board to make a Change in Recommendation or take any of the actions referred to in Section 5.02(b), except to the extent permitted by Section 5.02(b).   

COMMENT



A non-solicitation or "no-shop” provision is one of the deal protection provisions utilized to deter third parties from making a bid for the target between the date of the tender offer agreement and the closing of the tender offer/merger transaction and are included in some form in almost every public tender/merger agreement.  While in theory a target company may resist the inclusion of a no-shop provision and request that the purchaser instead rely on general remedies for breach of contract, it would be unusual for a purchaser to agree to do so, especially in light of the significant money, resources, opportunity cost and time that are required in order to pursue and complete any transaction. It is more likely that the no-shop is drafted to include various exceptions (as discussed below). In cases where the target company has significant bargaining power, it may be able to negotiate other favorable deal terms in exchange for its agreement to the terms and scope of the no-shop restrictions. 



Negotiating the No-Shop.  The no-shop provision must be evaluated in the context of the facts and circumstances of the particular transaction.  In that regard, there are many factors that should be considered by the target when evaluating and negotiating a no-shop, such as (i) whether the target board’s approval of the transaction and related deal protections will be reviewed under the business judgment rule or some form of enhanced scrutiny, (ii) whether and to what extent the target has previously been shopped, (iii) whether and to what extent voting agreements have been obtained from target stockholders, (iv) whether other deal protections are available and, if so, the relative strength of such deal protections, (v) whether the target board believes that the buyer’s offer is preemptive or otherwise at the high end of a range of fair values, (vi) whether and to what extent the target is able to obtain concessions from the buyer in exchange for the deal no-shop, and (vii) whether the target is in a precarious financial condition or is otherwise under strong pressure to be acquired.

There is an obvious tension between the interests of the purchaser and the interests of the target in negotiating the no-shop provision.  The purchaser’s primary interest is in deterring third parties from making a competing bid for the target, whereas the target’s primary interest is in having flexibility to entertain competing bids that might be more favorable to the target’s stockholders than the purchaser’s transaction.  As a result, the no-shop provision is typically one of the most heavily negotiated provisions in a merger agreement.  

No-Shop Restrictions. The no shop provision contained in Section 5.02(a) of the Model Agreement generally restricts the target company from (or directing its representatives in) soliciting, providing information to, or engaging in discussions or negotiations of an acquisition proposal by or with a third party.  Section 5.02(a) also includes a requirement that the target company cease any existing discussions with other parties concerning an acquisition transaction. 



Possible Changes to the No Shop that Might Be Proposed By Purchaser.  Given the importance and significance of the no-shop provision, it is likely that the purchaser will propose changes to a number of the terms of the no-shop. 



First, the purchaser may propose making the target strictly liable for any noncompliance of the no-shop by any of target’s representatives whether directed or not.  The target might argue that the target ultimately has no control over the actions of its representatives and can only "direct” its representatives to comply and not "authorize” any non-compliance.



Second, the purchaser may propose expanding the restrictions so as to forbidding the target or its representatives from "encouraging,” facilitating” or "taking any action” that could lead to an acquisition proposal.  The target might argue that these additional restrictions are too broad and excessively vague and ripe for the target to inadvertently or unknowingly breach the covenant.  The target could perhaps get comfortable with expanding the restrictions to cover actions that were "knowingly” or "actively” taken by the target. 



The purchaser may also propose expanding the definition of "Acquisition Proposal” to include "inquiries” or "indications of interests” relating to an Acquisition Transaction and to include in the definition of Acquisition Transactions proposed transactions (1) where the target is a buyer, (2) involving subsidiaries of the target, or (3) involving licenses of a portion of the target’s intellectual property.  The target will likely counter that the terms "inquiries” and "indications of interest” are vague and unlikely to cover anything that would likely interfere with the proposed transaction with the purchaser.  The target will also argue that Acquisition Transactions should not include subsidiaries (unless the target is merely a holding company for one or more operating subsidiaries) and certainly should not include minor subsidiaries.  



Window Shop.  A window shop provision, such as the one contained in the proviso to Section 5.02(a) of the Model Agreement, is an exception to the no-shop and generally permit the target board to furnish information to or enter into discussions with a third party who has made an acquisition proposal if the acquisition proposal is or likely to be a "superior proposal”.
