It is important to recognize that the typical window shop exception to a no-shop provision merely permits a target to provide information to and to talk to a third party that has submitted a potential competing bid.  It does not permit a target to solicit or initiate the making or submission of a competing bid or to sign an acquisition agreement with respect to a competing bid.



The term "Acquisition Proposal”, and the associated term "Acquisition Transaction,” are defined in the Model Agreement in a seller-favorable way in that it only includes (i) a possible acquisition transaction involving the target, and not any subsidiary of the target, (ii) a possible transaction in which the third party acquires more than 25% of the outstanding voting securities of the target, and (iii) asset sales and technology licenses constituting 25% or more of the target’s consolidated net revenues, net income, or assets. 



Possible Changes to the Window Shop that Might Be Proposed By Purchaser. The purchaser may propose limiting the window shop in a number of ways.  

First, the purchaser may argue that the target’s ability to furnish nonpublic information or enter into discussions with a third party in response to an Acquisition Proposal only apply if the Acquisition Proposal "is a Superior Proposal.”  However, the target may counter this argument by asserting that imposing a requirement that the Acquisition Proposal must constitute a Superior Proposal prior to discussions or the furnishing of information is too high a standard and that the third party will likely need access to confidential information and to have discussions with the target prior to making a definitive competing proposal.  The purchaser may also propose lowering the applicable percentages used in the definition of Acquisition Transaction (e.g., to 15%).

The purchaser may also propose providing that neither the target nor any of its representatives have violated any of the restrictions in Section 5.02 The target should limit this by proposing that the proposal did not directly result from a material breach of the restrictions of Section 5.02(a) as minor and unrelated breaches of the no-shop should not bar the target board from considering and negotiating a legitimate competing proposal. 

Third, the purchaser will likely propose that the target board have concluded in good faith, after having taken into account the advice or opinion of its outside legal counsel, that taking such action is required in order for the target board to comply with its fiduciary obligations to the target’s stockholders under applicable law.

Fourth, the purchaser may propose requiring that the confidentiality agreement to be entered into by the Person making the Acquisition Proposal be on terms (including a "standstill” undertaking) no less favorable than the terms contained in the confidentiality agreement between the purchaser and the target.

Fiduciary Out.  The no-shop provision in this Model Agreement includes a typical fiduciary out exception permitting the target to negotiate and complete a transaction with a third party and for the target board to change the its recommendation in favor of the transaction with the purchaser if the target board determines in good faith that failing to do so is reasonably likely to be inconsistent with its fiduciary duties to the target’s stockholders. In many cases the fiduciary out requires that the target board make a determination that the alternative acquisition proposal is a "superior proposal” before it can act without the no-shop restriction or terminate the tender agreement. 

If the purchaser has considerable leverage in the transaction and wants to take an aggressive "take it or leave it" position by offering a pure no-shop clause without exception, purchaser's counsel should consider the possibility that a court could invalidate, if challenged, the entire covenant (include cite). A no-shop that is too restrictive is generally not enforceable, except in very limited circumstances, because it prevents the target board from satisfying its fiduciary duties to the target stockholders.  As a result, the inclusion of a fiduciary out to a no-shop provision is market practice in public M&A transactions.



Matching rights are customarily included in tender and merger agreements, but the terms vary depending on the parties, their respective bargaining power and the transaction. Although it would be unusual for there to be no matching right, the target company should consider restricting the nature and terms of the purchaser’s right to have a "last look", and limit that right to only a one-time match. Limiting the match in this manner will increase the likelihood that the purchaser, given that it has only one opportunity to top the competing bid, is more likely to put forth its best counteroffer without having to go through several rounds of a protracted negotiation with each of the two competing bidders.



Section 5.02(b) of the Model Agreement provides that the target board may change its recommendation or enter into an agreement relating to an acquisition proposal from a third party if:



•	after having received an Acquisition Proposal, the target board has determined that the such Acquisition Proposal is, or is reasonably likely to lead to, a Superior Proposal; 

•	the target board has determined that the failure to effect the change in recommendation is reasonably likely to be inconsistent with its fiduciary obligations under applicable law;

•	the target has notified the purchaser of its intention to make the change in recommendation;

•	the target makes its representatives available during the three calendar days following delivery of such notice to discuss modifications to the terms of the tender offer agreement;

•	if purchaser delivers a binding offer to amend the terms of the tender offer agreement during the three calendar day period, the target board has again determined that the failure to effect the change in recommendation to be inconsistent with its fiduciary duties.

The Model Agreement also includes that ability of the target company to change its recommendation upon becoming aware of an intervening event or circumstance that the target board was unaware of at the signing of the agreement that makes it not advisable to complete the transaction. The purchaser may argue against the inclusion of this exception to the no-shop provision because it is overly broad and perhaps not necessary under applicable legal requirements. The purchaser could also argue that if there is an intervening event and the proposed transaction is no longer favorable, then the target stockholders would simply not tender their shares and the minimum condition would not be satisfied. 



Possible Changes to the Fiduciary Exception that Might Be Proposed By Purchaser.  Depending on the circumstances, the purchaser might propose a number of changes to the fiduciary exception contained in Section 5.02(a).

First, the purchaser might have a number of comments with respect to the definition of "Superior Proposal” contained in Section 9.6.  The purchaser may suggest that only proposals for all of the outstanding shares of common stock, or all or substantially all of the assets, of the target should qualify as a "Superior Proposal” if the other requirements contained in the definition are also satisfied.  The purchaser might also argue that the target board’s determination as to whether a proposal constitutes a "Superior Proposal” should be based on a higher standard, such as the target board’s reasonable judgment, rather than the target board’s good faith. 

A second objection that the purchaser may raise in relation to the definition of "Superior Proposal” might be that the target board’s determination be based on a written opinion of a financial advisor.  However, the target could argue that because of the inherent uncertainties in rendering such an opinion, it might be difficult and costly to obtain such an opinion.  Furthermore, there is Delaware case law indicating that a board is not obligated to heed the counsel or advice of any of its advisors and must make its own determination. 

A final issue with the term "Superior Proposal” is what conditions beyond financial superiority must be satisfied for a competing proposal to be deemed a Superior Proposal.  The purchaser may propose that the definition of Superior Proposal include a condition that any financing required to consummate the competing proposal must be committed and be reasonably capable of being obtained.  A target might object to this additional requirement as to the financing on the ground that so long as the target board believes that the transaction is reasonably capable of being consummated, the specifics with regard to the financing should only go to the target board’s determination of the financial superiority of the proposal.  The purchaser might also require that the target board take into account the identity of the person making the proposal.  

The purchaser may try to increase the time period required for the purchaser company to give notice of its intent to exercise its matching right. The purchaser will likely argue that it needs more time in order for its board to consider and formulate a response to the competing bid, and to negotiate any necessary changes to its financing arrangements.  



Further, the purchaser target might seek to limit the fiduciary exception y providing that the target company cannot use the fiduciary exception if there has been a breach of the no-shop undertaking.  The target company will likely counter this argument by arguing that while a violation by the target company or its representatives of the no-shop might give rise to a failure of a condition or breach of contract claim or a termination right, the ability of the target company to provide information or enter into discussions with a third party should not depend on whether the target company violated any of the no-shop restrictions.  By way of example, the target company might argue that even if it violated the no-shop by not providing the buyer with the required notice of an acquisition proposal that it received from a third party, it should not be prohibited from providing information to a different third party in response to its acquisition proposal.  The target might also argue that any breach must be material, intentional, or both.  

Prohibition on Release of Standstill.  The purchaser may propose that the target company be prohibited from releasing any person from any confidentiality or "standstill” agreement entered into by the target company in connection with a possible merger or acquisition transaction and requires the target to enforce such confidentiality and standstill provisions at the request of the buyer.  If so, the target might object to this requirement and argue that the target board should have the right to make such a waiver if it determines, after consultation with its legal counsel, that it is necessary to release a third party from a standstill agreement in order to comply with its fiduciary duties to the target stockholders.  The purchaser may also require that the target be required to request from every party that signed such a confidentiality or standstill agreement in connection with a possible merger or acquisition transaction prior to the signing of the tender agreement return all confidential information provided by the target to the third party because it does not want any potential bidder to remain in possession of confidential information.  The target might argue that the requirement is too onerous or unnecessary given that the third party continues to be bound by the confidentiality undertaking.  

Compliance with Rules 14d-9, 14e-2(a) and Item 1012(a).  Section 5.02(e) of the Model Agreement permits the target board to comply with Rule 14e-2(a), Rule 14d-9 and Item 1012(a) under the Exchange Act, provided that the board cannot take any action which would constitute a Change in Recommendation without complying with the additional requirements of Section 5.02.  Rule 14e-2(a) of the Exchange Act requires the target to publish, within 10 business days following the commencement of a tender offer with respect to it, a statement disclosing whether the target (i) recommends acceptance or rejection of the tender offer, (ii) expresses no opinion and is remaining neutral toward the tender offer, or (iii) is unable to take a position with respect to the tender offer.  Rule 14e-2(a) further requires the target to include the reasons for the position disclosed pursuant to the foregoing.  Rule 14d-9 of the Exchange Act governs communications by the target with respect to the tender offer to which it is subject.  Specifically, Rule 14d-9(b) prohibits the target board from soliciting or making a recommendation to its security holders until a Schedule 14D-9 is filed with the SEC containing the target board’s recommendation as required under Rule 14e-2(a).  In addition, Rule 14d-9(f) permits the target board to issue a "stop, look and listen” release, stating that, among other things, the tender offer is under consideration by the target board and that the Company’s stockholders are requested to defer making a determination whether to accept or reject the tender offer until it has been advised of the target board’s position.  Item 1012(a) permits more disclosure than expressly permitted under Rule 14d-9 or Rule 14e-2, including describing actions recommended by the target board beyond the statement of the target board’s position.  

Other Possible Exceptions to the No Shop

Go Shop.  

A go-shop is another exception to the no-shop restrictions that specifically allows the target company to seek out other potential bidders for a specified period of time, usually between 30 to 60 days after the date of signing of the tender agreement. Go-shop provisions are sometimes considered in connection with transactions in which the target company has not conducted an auction or done a pre signing market check and the target board has potential concerns about satisfying its Revlon duties, such as a management buyout, or single bidder situations.  Go-shops are primarily found in private equity transactions because private equity buyers tend to prefer avoiding a full auction process, especially the potential of competing against strategic companies.  



Go shops typically include the right to match a superior proposal received during the go-shop period (in a manner similar to the fiduciary out discussed above), (ii) usually have a lower break-up fee payable by the target company if it terminates the tender agreement due to a superior proposal received during the go-shop period, and (ii) frequently, the right to continue to discussions or negotiations with any competing bidders that arise during the go-shop period. 



ARTICLE 6

ADDITIONAL AGREEMENTS

6.01.Ti=	Access and Investigation.  

6.01.(1).sec=	During the period from the date of this Agreement through the Effective Time or the earlier termination of this Agreement in accordance with Article VIII hereof, the Company shall, and shall cause the Representatives of the Company and its Subsidiaries to: 

6.01.(1).(1).sec=	provide Parent and Parent’s Representatives with reasonable access (during regular business hours) to the personnel, assets, books, records, and Tax Returns of the Company and its Subsidiaries as Parent may from time to time reasonably request; provided, that any such access shall be conducted at a reasonable time, upon reasonable advance notice to the Company and in such a manner as not to interfere unreasonably with the operation of any business conducted by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries; and 

6.01.(1).(2).sec=	cause its officers and those of its Subsidiaries to furnish Parent with such financial and operating data and other information with respect to the business, properties and personnel of the Company and its Subsidiaries as Parent or Purchaser may from time to time reasonably request; 

[provided, that no access or information pursuant to this Section 6.01 shall affect or be deemed to modify any representation or warranty made or deemed made by the Company herein].  [NTD:  Delete for seller-friendly first draft?]  The information obtained by Parent pursuant to this Section 6.01(a) shall be subject to the provisions of the Confidentiality Agreement.

6.01.(2).sec=	Nothing in this Section 6.01 shall require the Company to permit any inspection, or to disclose 

6.01.(2).(1).sec=	any information concerning Acquisition Proposals, which shall be governed by Section 5.02, 

6.01.(2).(2).sec=	any information regarding the deliberations of the Company Board with respect to the Contemplated Transactions, the entry into the Agreement or any materials provided to the Company Board in connection therewith, 

6.01.(2).(3).sec=	materials prepared by the Company’s financial, accounting, or legal advisors or which is subject to an attorney/client or an attorney work product privilege, or

6.01.(2).(4).sec=	any information that in the reasonable judgment of the Company would (x) violate any of its respective obligations with respect to confidentiality, provided, that the Company shall use its commercially reasonable efforts to obtain the consent of such third party to such inspection or disclosure, or (y) result in a violation of any applicable Legal Requirement, including Federal or state securities, antitrust or privacy laws.

COMMENT:

During the pre-closing period, Parent will seek to be informed about developments that may have a material impact on the Company.  Parent in particular needs access to appropriate information so that it is in as good a position as possible to evaluate the accuracy of the Company’s representations and warranties and to determine whether it desires, and is obligated, to continue with or consummate the Offer.  This is important both at the closing and prior to the closing, since Parent has the right to terminate the Model Agreement if there has been a breach of a representation or warranty of the Company that is not cured within a specified period (see Section 8.01(g) of the Model Agreement).  Parent needs these rights both prior to the Acceptance Time and during the period in between the Acceptance Time and the Effective Time, which could be an extended period of time if Parent does not obtain a sufficient number of the shares of Company Common Stock to complete a short-form second step merger pursuant to DGCL Section 253 or Section 267. 

Even if the information does not relate directly to Parent’s specific rights under the Agreement, if Parent has timely knowledge of events it will have more of an opportunity to consult with the Company and can better plan for contingencies.  

This covenant also supports Parent’s preparations for integrating the two organizations after the closing.  As one example, information about the Company must be included in Parent’s SEC filings covering any post-closing period.  Given the certifications that Parent’s chief executive officer and chief financial officer must file with the SEC pursuant to Sections 302 and 906 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act, Parent will seek to use the pre-closing period to evaluate in more detail the adequacy of the Company’s internal financial controls and disclosure controls and procedures. 

Limits on Access.  Section 6.01(b) addresses the Company’s interest in preventing regulatory and other legal problems, such as antitrust gun-jumping (discussed in further detail below), associated with providing access to Parent.  The Company has an interest in preventing these problems whether a deal closes or not.  Parent also has an interest in preventing these problems, as Parent will suffer from the adverse consequences if it completes the acquisition and acquires the Company; however, Parent does not want to allow these concerns to act as an undue barrier to receiving information.  With respect to obligations of confidentiality, the Company has provided that it will use its commercially reasonable efforts to obtain consent of third parties.  The parties may be able to take steps to address concerns relating to attorney client privilege by entering into a joint defense agreement.  

The Company generally will want to make clear that it is not required to share information with respect to the deliberations of the Company Board in connection with the execution of the Model Agreement, such as board minutes and presentations.  Similarly, the Company will also want to ensure that any obligations it has to provide information with respect to Acquisition Proposals be governed by the non-solicitation covenant in Section 5.02. 

Antitrust Gun-Jumping.  Although the parties have agreed to merge, the antitrust laws will continue to regulate competitive activities until the merger is consummated.  Accordingly, appropriate care must be taken in the parties’ exchange of competitively sensitive information.  Drawing the line in this area is not always easy, but great caution should be exercised with respect to any exchange of information regarding open contract bids, bidding or pricing practices, pricing or specific marketing plans and other comparable information.  Exchanges of information among competitors can give rise to serious concern that those agreements evidence an agreement in restraint of trade.  The parties likely will have faced similar issues when conducting due diligence prior to execution of the Model Agreement.

The risk of violating antitrust laws may be mitigated by taking steps to control the dissemination and use of the information within Parent, such as by:

•	Limiting the information exchanged to that truly needed for due diligence or integration planning.

•	Timing the information exchange so that it occurs only when the need for the information is clear.

•	Restricting the recipients of the information to those within Parent with a clear need to know and avoiding the provision of the information to employees charged with responsibility for competitive decision-making.  To provide a clear record of such safeguards, a written undertaking by Parent to restrict the dissemination of sensitive information may be advisable.

•	Conducting due diligence in more competitively sensitive areas through third party intermediaries who are put under confidentiality agreements.  These third-party intermediaries can then assess the competitively sensitive information, and advise the party they represent of the implications of the information reviewed, without revealing the specific details of the sensitive information in a manner raising antitrust concern.  This will allow confirmatory due diligence to proceed while shielding the two competitors from access to information presenting the most antitrust risk.

These steps also can help reduce the business risk inherent in exchanging information with a buyer who is or may be a competitor to the Company.

Impact on Representations and Warranties.  The parties will carefully negotiate a set of representations and warranties that will be made by the Company as part of the Agreement.  The representations and warranties serve a number of purposes, including the allocation of risk between the Company and Parent.  It is important for both parties that that information the Company provides to Parent pursuant to Section 6.01 not modify these representations and warranties.  For example, the Company generally wants to avoid any implication that it is representing and warranting to the accuracy of any reports or documents given to Parent in response to an information request.  Similarly, Parent generally will want to avoid a scenario where the Company may update its representations and warranties and potentially cure breaches by providing information pursuant to this covenant.  [The proviso at the end of the first sentence of Section 6.01(a) addresses this concern by stating that no access or information provided pursuant to Section 6.01 shall modify any of the Company’s representations and warranties.] [NTD:  Conform to placement in text as initial text or Purchaser comment.]

Possible Changes To The Access Covenant That Might Be Suggested by Parent.  Parent may have a number of comments to this provision, such as the following:  

First, Parent will generally try to expand the scope of materials covered by the covenant.  In addition to the items already covered, Parent may want the Company to provide it with access to work papers and other documents, and additional financial, operating and other data and information regarding the Company.  The Company may resist granting Parent access to auditor work papers, as it will not be able to force its auditors to deliver those work papers to Parent.  At a minimum, the Company would likely insist that access to work papers be conditioned on Parent entering into a customary confidentiality agreement that is acceptable to the Company’s auditors.  [Relatedly, while this is arguable already covered, Parent may want to explicitly require that its access to any virtual data rooms or other diligence materials continue uninterrupted.]  [NTD:  Please elaborate.]

Second, Parent may remove some of the express limits in Section 6.01(b) and argue that the agreement should leave those issues for Parent to consider in making its requests for information.  If the transaction closes, the adverse consequences created by the disclosures will be Parent’s problems going forward.  In the alternative, Parent may seek to impose an obligation on the Company to find alternative means to provide information to avoid the consequences set forth in Section 6.01(b), as the provision does with respect to information subject to a confidentiality undertaking. 

Third, Parent may insert affirmative obligations to provide information, such as requiring the Company to provide Parent with all material operating and financial reports prepared for the Company’s management, including copies of any unaudited monthly consolidated financial statements.  Similarly, Parent may also want an affirmative right to meet and interview employees of the Company, especially in situations where Parent has not had the ability to conduct the requisite amount of diligence prior to execution of the Model Agreement.  The Company, if it is to accept such an obligation, may seek to qualify this right with a reasonableness standard.

Fourth, Parent may want to require the Company to consult with outside counsel in connection with its determination that applicable law or a confidentiality restriction prohibits the sharing of information with Parent.  This requirement may give Parent comfort that the Company will at the very least need to consult with a qualified third party prior to making the determination that there is a legal prohibition with sharing the information.  If Parent wanted to be aggressive, it could require that the Company not only consult with outside counsel but that is also receive the advice of outside counsel that such a legal prohibition exists.  The Company may resist such a requirement as it could impose a level of formality and costs associated with retaining counsel that is overly burdensome.

6.02.Ti=	Notification.  

During the Pre-Closing Period, each Party shall promptly notify the other Parties of the occurrence, or non-occurrence, of any event that would reasonably be expected to result in any condition to the obligations of any Party to effect any of the Contemplated Transactions not to be satisfied.  No notification pursuant to this Section 6.02 shall limit or otherwise affect any of the representations, warranties, covenants or obligations of the Parties contained in this Agreement.

COMMENT:

This covenant requires each of the parties to notify the others upon the occurrence of any event, including a breach of a representation, warranty or covenant, that would cause a closing condition to not be satisfied.  As a practical matter, this covenant will be of more concern to the Company than Parent given the number of representations and warranties made by the Company in the merger agreement and the fact that most of the covenants apply to actions it is required to take or prohibited from taking prior to closing. 

Possible Changes To The Notification Covenant That Might Be Suggested by Parent.  Parent may seek to increase the scope of the obligation of the Company to provide notice beyond those events that would cause closing conditions to be satisfied.  Generally, the bring down of the representations and warranties of the Company is subject to a material adverse effect standard, and Parent may want the Company to notify it of breaches that are material but which do not satisfy that high standard in order to make plans for the Company following the closing and to get an accurate picture of the Company.  The Company may resist this expansion on the basis that Parent should only be entitled to notices of breaches that would give it the right to not close and to terminate the merger agreement.  

6.03.Ti=	[Proxy Statement [or Information Statement].]  

6.03.(1).sec=	If after the Acceptance Time and, to the extent applicable, any Subsequent Offering Period, the adoption of this Agreement by the Company’s stockholders is required by applicable Legal Requirements to consummate the Merger, the Company shall prepare the Proxy Statement and cause it to be filed with the SEC [or, if Parent specifies that adoption of this Agreement be effected by the written consent of the stockholders of the Company without a meeting (the "Stockholder Consent”), the Company shall prepare an information statement with respect to the Stockholder Consent (the "Information Statement”)].  Parent shall furnish to the Company all information concerning it and Purchaser and their respective officers, directors, Affiliates and agents as the Company may reasonably request in connection with the preparation of the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] and any amendment thereto and shall otherwise assist and cooperate with the Company in the preparation of the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] and the resolution of comments (if any) to the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] referred to below.  Parent and the Company shall each use commercially reasonable efforts to cause the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] to comply with the rules and regulations promulgated by the SEC and to respond promptly to any comments of the SEC or its staff and to comply as to form and substance in all material respects with the applicable requirements of the Exchange Act.

6.03.(2).sec=	The Company, on the one hand, and Parent and Purchaser, on the other hand, agree to promptly correct any information provided by it for use in the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] if and to the extent that it shall have become false or misleading in any material respect or as otherwise required by applicable Legal Requirements.

6.03.(3).sec=	The Company will advise Parent, promptly after it receives notice thereof, of any request by the staff of the SEC for amendment of the Proxy Statement [or Information Statement, as applicable,] or comments thereon or responses thereto.

COMMENT:

In Article II of the Agreement, Purchaser has agreed to consummate a second-step merger following the completion of the tender offer.  Because this Agreement is governed by Section 251(h) of the DGCL, no vote is required to adopt the second-step merger, and this Section may be omitted.  Nonetheless, this Section is included in this Model Agreement to provide example and discussion in the event an agreement is not governed by DGCL Section 251(h).  See generally Comment to Recitals.

If DGCL Section 251(h) is inapplicable and Purchaser owns 90% or more of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock, after completing any subsequent offering period and exercising the top-up option, Purchaser can complete a short form merger.  If Purchaser does not acquire 90% or more of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock, completion of the second step merger will require the Company to convene a meeting of its stockholders or, if permitted by the Company’s organizational documents, for the Company’s stockholders to act by written consent, in each case, to adopt the merger agreement.  

Pursuant to DGCL Section 251, a merger not governed by DGCL Section 251(h) must be submitted to a vote of the Company’s stockholders at an annual or special meeting called for that purpose.  Under the DGCL, stockholders must be given at least 20 days prior notice of the meeting.  The solicitation by the Company of its stockholders for votes in favor of the merger will be subject to the federal proxy rules, which require that Company to prepare proxy solicitation materials and obtain clearance of the materials from the SEC prior to delivering such materials to its stockholders.  The instructions to Schedule 14A require that the proxy solicitation materials be mailed to stockholders of the Company no later than 20 business days prior to the date of the meeting if the Company incorporates by reference any document or portion or a document other than its annual report into the proxy statement.  As it is routine practice to incorporate documents by reference into a proxy statement, the practical effect of this instruction is to require the Company stockholder meeting to take place at least 20 business days following the mailing of the proxy statement.  

If permitted by the Company’s articles of incorporation and applicable state law, the second-step merger may also be approved by written consent in lieu of a meeting of stockholders.  For Delaware corporations, DGCL Section 228 provides that stockholders may take action by written consent unless otherwise provided in the Company’s certificate of incorporation.  DGCL Section 228 permits corporate action without a meeting, without prior notice and without a vote, if a consent in writing is executed by the holders of stock having sufficient votes to authorize such action at a meeting.  Following consummation of the Offer, Purchaser would have sufficient shares to approve the second-step Merger by written consent without the action of any other stockholder.  

The taking of action by written consent to approve a second-step merger is subject to Rule 14C under the Securities Exchange Act.  Rule 14C-2 requires an information statement to be sent to the Company’s stockholders at least 20 days prior to the effectiveness of the action by written consent, even if the Company does not solicit the consent of its stockholders.  A preliminary copy of the information statement must be filed with the SEC at least 10 days prior to the date definitive copies are sent to the Company’s stockholders.

For a discussion of the use of either a proxy statement or information statement as a notice of appraisal rights, see Comment to Section 1.02.

Section 6.03, in combination with Section 6.04, sets forth the parties’ contractual commitments to take the steps required to complete the second-step Merger.  Section 6.03 obligates the Company to prepare and file a proxy statement or information statement if approval of the Company’s stockholders is required to complete the Merger.  The parties preferred outcome is that Purchaser acquires a sufficient number of the Company’s shares through the Offer and top-up option to complete a short-form second step Merger, in which case no proxy or information statement will be required.  

"Dual Track” Tender Offer and Merger Filings.  From a timing perspective, the Company is typically only obligated to prepare and file a proxy or information statement after the Acceptance Time and any Subsequent Offering Period, so that the substantial effort required to complete the proxy statement or information statement is only undertaken if necessary.  However, in a number of recent transactions the parties have agreed to prepare and file a proxy statement or information statement prior to completion of the Offer.  In those cases, the parties use a "dual track” structure whereby completion of the transaction through a tender offer followed by a merger advances alongside efforts to complete the transaction through a traditional one-step merger.  If Parent does not obtain a sufficient number of the Company’s shares through the tender offer to complete a short-form second step merger, the "dual track” structure minimizes the delay associated with preparing the proxy statement and convening a stockholder meeting in order to obtain stockholder approval for the merger. 

The dual track structure has become increasingly used in front end tender offer transactions where the minimum condition is set far in excess of a majority of outstanding shares.  This is the case where the acquiror is a private equity firm and due to its financing requirements, it needs to acquire sufficient shares (when combined with the top-up option) to consummate the short form merger concurrently with or very shortly after the closing of the tender offer.  As a result of these constraints, the minimum condition will be set at that percentage of shares which will only require the acquiror to consummate the tender offer at a level which ensures that it will also be able to consummate a short form merger.  If this minimum condition percentage is sufficiently high, the parties may wish to have the more traditional single step merger process started as a back-up plan in the event that the high number of shares to satisfy the condition is not met.  In the event the dual track structure is used, the closing conditions will need to be modified to include more traditional single-step merger closing conditions, such as accuracy of representations and warranties and compliance with covenants.  [NTD:  Add reference to SEC 14e-5 position.]

Parent Review.  The obligation to prepare and file the proxy or information statement falls upon the Company.  Parent has a significant interest in ensuring that the Company files the proxy or information statement as promptly as practicable and in compliance with all applicable SEC requirements.  In its comments on this covenant, Parent can add language to 6.03(a) to specify that the Company will prepare and file the proxy statement or information statement as promptly as practicable following the Acceptance Time and any Subsequent Offering Period.  Parent can also ask for the right to review and comment on the proxy statement or information statement before it is filed with the SEC.  Similarly, while Section 6.03(c) provides that the Company will advise Parent of the receipt of any SEC comments, Parent may prefer to receive copies of any such comments, to the extent they are in writing, and to be informed of the substance of all such comments, to the extent that they are not in writing.  Parent also may want to review and comment on any responses to be submitted in response to such comments.  

6.04.Ti=	[[Written Consent of Stockholders; ]Company Stockholders’ Meeting.]  

6.04.(1).sec=	Unless the Merger is consummated in accordance with Section 253 of the DGCL as contemplated by Section 6.04(b), promptly following the Acceptance Time and, to the extent applicable, any Subsequent Offering Period, Parent shall promptly notify the Company whether Parent and/or its Affiliates elect to adopt this Agreement by executing and delivering the Stockholder Consent as the holders of a majority of the issued and outstanding shares of Company Common Stock, in which case, the Company, acting through the Company Board, shall, in accordance with and subject to the requirements of applicable Legal Requirements: 

6.04.(1).(1).sec=	 as promptly as practicable after the Acceptance Time, set a record date for the Stockholder Consent for the purpose of adopting this Agreement; 

6.04.(1).(2).sec=	as promptly as practicable after the execution and delivery of the Stockholder Consent, file the Information Statement with the SEC and cause the Information Statement to be printed and mailed to the stockholders of the Company; and 

6.04.(1).(3).sec=	as promptly as practicable after the Company is legally permitted to do so under applicable Legal Requirements, consummate the actions approved in the Stockholder Consent.  

If Parent elects to adopt this Agreement by executing an action by written consent, Parent and Merger Sub shall promptly execute, or cause to be executed, the Stockholder Consent with respect to all of the shares of Company Common Stock then owed of record by Parent and its Affiliates or with respect to which Parent or any of its Affiliates otherwise has, directly or indirectly, sole voting power.]

6.04.(2).sec=	If the adoption of this Agreement by the Company’s stockholders is required by applicable Legal Requirements to consummate the Merger, then[, if Parent does not specify that adoption of this Agreement be effected by Stockholder Consent,] the Company shall, as promptly as reasonably practicable after receipt of SEC clearance of the Proxy Statement, establish a record date for, call, give notice of (and cause the Proxy Statement to be mailed to its stockholders), and hold a meeting of its stockholders to vote on a proposal to approve and adopt this Agreement and the Merger (the "Company Stockholders’ Meeting”).  The Company Stockholders’ Meeting shall be held as promptly as practicable after the Acceptance Time (or, as applicable, after the consummation of any Subsequent Offering Period).  Subject to Section 5.02(b), the Proxy Statement shall include the Board Recommendation. At the Company Stockholders’ Meeting, Parent shall vote, or cause to be voted, all of the shares of Company Common Stock then owned by it, Purchaser, Merger Sub or any of their other Affiliates in favor of the adoption of this Agreement.   

Notwithstanding the foregoing, if, following the Acceptance Time (or, as applicable, after the consummation of any Subsequent Offering Period) and the exercise, if any, of the Top-Up Option, Parent and its Affiliates shall own at least 90% of the outstanding shares of the Company Common Stock, the Parties shall take all necessary and appropriate action, including with respect to the transfer to Purchaser of any shares of Company Common Stock held by Parent or its Affiliates, to cause the Merger to become effective as soon as practicable thereafter without the Company Stockholders’ Meeting in accordance with Section 253 of the DGCL.

COMMENT:

The covenants in Section 6.04 complement the covenants in Section 6.03, which together require the parties to take the steps necessary to complete the second-step Merger.  Because this Agreement is governed by Section 251(h) of the DGCL, no vote is required to adopt the second-step merger, and this Section may be omitted.  Nonetheless, this Section is included in this Model Agreement to provide example and discussion in the event an agreement is not governed by Section 251(h).  See generally Comment to Recitals.

Section 6.03 addresses the preparation and filing with the SEC of a proxy statement or information statement.  Section 6.04 addresses the other actions required to approve the second-step Merger.  Pursuant to Section 6.04, if Parent and its Affiliates obtain a sufficient number of shares of Company Common Stock to consummate a short-form second-step Merger pursuant to DGCL Section 253 or Section 267, they are required to do so as soon as practicable.  

If Parent does not obtain a sufficient number of shares of Company Common Stock to consummate a short-form second-step Merger, Parent is given the right to elect whether to act by written consent or to have the Company call a meeting of its stockholders.  Parent must promptly notify the Company whether it chooses to exercise its election to act by written consent so that the Company can proceed according to the appropriate course of action.  If Parent elects to act by written consent, it must promptly deliver an executed consent to the Company.  If a meeting of the Company’s stockholders is convened, Parent is required to vote in favor of adoption of the Agreement. 

Section 6.04(b) requires that the Proxy Statement include the recommendation of the Company Board that the Company’s stockholders vote in favor of the adoption of this Agreement.  This requirement is subject to Section 5.02(b), which sets forth the standard for the Company Board to effect a Change in Recommendation.  

6.05.Ti=	Reasonable Best Efforts; Regulatory Approvals.  

6.05.(1).sec=	Without limiting the generality of anything contained in this Section 6.05, Parent and Purchaser shall use reasonable best efforts to cause all Offer Conditions to be satisfied on a timely basis (to the extent the satisfaction of such Offer Conditions is within Parent’s or Purchaser’s direct or indirect control) and to cause Purchaser to purchase shares of the Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer on the earliest possible date.  In furtherance and not in limitation of the foregoing, each of Parent and Purchaser, and each of Parent and Purchaser shall cause their respective Affiliates, if applicable, to: (i) promptly after the date of this Agreement prepare and, in no event later than five business days after the date of this Agreement, file any and all notices, reports and other documents required to be filed by such party under the HSR Act and any applicable foreign Antitrust Laws with respect to the Offer, the Merger and the other Contemplated Transactions; (ii) use reasonable best efforts promptly to cause the expiration or termination of any applicable waiting periods under the HSR Act and any applicable foreign Antitrust Laws; (iii) promptly respond to all inquiries or requests from any Governmental Body in connection with the Contemplated Transactions; and (iv) use reasonable best efforts to cause to be taken, on a timely basis, all other actions necessary or appropriate for the purpose of consummating and effectuating the Contemplated Transactions.

6.05.(2).sec=	Each Party shall, subject to applicable Legal Requirements and except as prohibited by any applicable representative of any applicable Governmental Body:

6.05.(2).(1).sec=	give the other Parties prompt notice of the commencement or threat of commencement of any Legal Proceeding by or before any Governmental Body with respect to the Offer, the Merger or any of the other Contemplated Transactions,

6.05.(2).(2).sec=	keep the other Party informed as to the status of any such Legal Proceeding or threat,

6.05.(2).(3).sec=	promptly inform the other party of any material communication concerning Antitrust Laws to or from any Governmental Body regarding the Offer, the Merger or any of the Contemplated Transactions,

6.05.(2).(4).sec=	consult and cooperate with one another, and consider in good faith the views of one another, in connection with any analysis, appearance, presentation, memorandum, brief, argument, opinion or proposal made or submitted in connection with any Legal Proceeding under or relating to the HSR Act or any other Antitrust Law, and permit the other party to review any such proposal or submission in advance,

6.05.(2).(5).sec=	not participate in or agree to participate in any substantive meeting or discussion with any Governmental Body in respect of any filings, investigation or inquiry concerning this Agreement, the Offer, the Merger or the other Contemplated Transactions unless it consults with the other parties in advance and, to the extent permitted by such Governmental Body, gives the other party the opportunity to attend and participate thereat, and

6.05.(2).(6).sec=	promptly take, and cause its Affiliates to take, all actions and steps requested or required by any Governmental Body as a condition to granting any consent, permit, authorization, waiver, clearance, approvals and expirations or terminations of waiting periods with respect to the Contemplated Transactions or to avoid the entry of, or to effect the dissolution of, any injunction, temporary restraining order or other order in any Legal Proceeding which would otherwise have the effect of preventing the Closing, materially delaying the Acceptance Time or the Closing or delaying the Acceptance Time beyond the Expiration Date, including 

(x)	negotiating, committing to and effecting, by consent decree, hold separate order or otherwise, the sale, lease, license, divestiture or disposition of any assets, rights, product lines, or businesses of Parent or its Subsidiaries or the Company or its Subsidiaries and 

(y)	otherwise taking or committing to take any actions that after the Closing Date limits the freedom of Parent or its Subsidiaries’ (including the Surviving Corporation’s) freedom of action with respect to, or its ability to retain, one or more of its or its Subsidiaries’ (including the Surviving Corporation’s) businesses, product lines or assets, 

provided, that the Company and its Subsidiaries will only be required to take or commit to take any such action, or agree to any such condition or restriction, if such action, commitment, agreement, condition or restriction is binding on the Company and its Subsidiaries only following the Acceptance Time.  

The entry by any Governmental Body in any Legal Proceeding of an Order requiring any of the businesses, product lines or assets of Parent or any of its Subsidiaries to be divested, held separate, or otherwise be legally or commercially limited thereafter (including the businesses, product lines and assets of the Company and its Subsidiaries after the Acceptance Time) shall not be deemed to constitute or result in a breach of any representation, warranty or covenant in this Agreement or a failure of any closing condition to be satisfied.

6.05.(3).sec=	Nothing contained in this Agreement shall give Parent or Purchaser, directly or indirectly, the right to control or direct the operations of the Company prior to the Acceptance Time.  Prior to the Acceptance Time, the Company shall exercise, consistent with the terms and conditions of this Agreement, complete unilateral control and supervision over its business operations.

6.06.Ti=	Disclosure.  

The Parties shall consult with each other before issuing any press release or otherwise making any public statement or disclosure with respect to the Offer, the Merger or any of the other Contemplated Transactions without the prior approval of the other Parties (which approval shall not be unreasonably withheld, conditioned or delayed).  Notwithstanding the foregoing:

6.06.(1).sec=	each Party may, without such consultation or consent, make any public statement in response to questions from the press, analysts, investors or those attending industry conferences, make internal announcements to employees and make disclosures in Company SEC Reports, so long as such statements are consistent with previous press releases, public disclosures or public statements made jointly by the Parties (or individually, if approved by the other Parties),

6.06.(2).sec=	a Party may, without the prior consent of the other Parties, issue any such press release or make any such public announcement or statement as may be required by any applicable Legal Requirement or by obligations pursuant to any listing agreement with any national securities exchange; provided, that the Party proposing to issue such press release or make such public announcement or statement shall first, to the extent practicable, consult with the other Parties about, and allow the other Parties reasonable time to comment in advance on, such press release, public announcement or statement; and

6.06.(3).sec=	the Company need not consult with Parent in connection with any press release, public statement or filing to be issued or made with respect to any Acquisition Proposal (including any "stop, look and listen” release), Superior Proposal or Change in Recommendation.

COMMENT:

This covenant requires prior consultation and approval between the parties before either can make press releases or other public statements regarding the Offer and the Merger.  This covenant is designed to assure that consistent information is given by the parties to the public markets regarding the terms of the transaction and that such communications are consistent with the disclosures made in the tender offer documents filed with the SEC.  

Note that this requirement would apply to all public disclosures about the transaction, including the press release announcing the transaction, and all subsequent public disclosures, including information that has already been disclosed and which is republished or otherwise made available again.  As both parties are public companies, situations may arise where one party may be required under federal securities laws to make a public disclosure before it can obtain the consent of the other party.  Section 6.06 addresses this issue by permitting the party to make disclosures that are legally required or required by any listing rules to which it is subject and imposing only the requirement that it consult to the extent practicable, with the non-disclosing party in advance.  Additionally, in order to minimize the number of times the Parties need to consult with each other regarding the disclosure of the same information but in different formats, which can be a time consuming process, the covenant contains an exception allowing the parties to make public statements without the need to consult with the other to the extent such disclosure is consistent with prior disclosures jointly made by the parties or made by one party with the approval of the other.  

Finally, the covenant contains an exception for the Company to communicate with its stockholders without the need to consult with Parent for matters relating to Acquisition Proposals, Superior Proposals and Changes in Recommendation.  Parent will likely require the carveout for such communications to be subject the requirements set forth in the non-solicitation covenant and also to make clear that while the Company has the freedom to make such disclosures, that freedom does not nullify any rights Parent may have with respect to the disclosure, including that disclosure may constitute a Change of Recommendation or endorsement of a Superior Proposal and permit Parent to take certain actions based thereon.

6.07.Ti=	Transfer Taxes.  

Parent shall pay, or cause to be paid, all documentary, sales, use, real property transfer, registration, transfer, stamp, recording and similar Taxes, fees, and costs together with any interest thereon, penalties, fines, costs, fees, additions to tax or additional amounts with respect thereto incurred in connection with this Agreement and the Contemplated Transactions, and shall file all Tax Returns related thereto that are required to be filed by Parent.

6.08.Ti=	Resignation of Directors.  

The Company shall use commercially reasonable efforts to obtain and deliver to Parent prior to the Closing Date (to be effective as of the Effective Time) the resignation of each director of the Company and each of its Subsidiaries (in each case, in their capacities as directors, and not as employees) as Parent shall request in writing not less than five days prior to the Closing Date.

COMMENT:

Upon completion of the Merger, the Company will be a wholly owned subsidiary of Parent.  Having resignations in hand from the directors of the Company, as well as all subsidiaries of the Company, will facilitate Parent’s ability to appoint its own directors and officers.  Because the Company does not directly control its directors, it can only request their resignations, not require them, so it is being asked only to use "commercially reasonable efforts” to obtain them. This covenant should be read together with Section 1.04, which permits Parent to appoint its nominees to the Company board of directors following consummation of the Offer in proportion to the percentage of Company Common Stock it owns, and Section 2.8 of the Agreement, which provides that the directors and officers of Purchaser will become directors and officers of the surviving corporation at the effective time.  

The Company may resist inclusion of the covenant on the grounds that it does not want to ask its directors to resign and that following consummation of the Merger, Parent will be the sole stockholder of the surviving company and will have the power to remove and replace directors (assuming the organizational documents of the surviving corporation that are put into place at closing of the Merger permit it to do so).  Parent may counter that the Company has already agreed to cause the directors to resign in connection with the appointment of Parent’s nominees at the consummation of the Offer and should be willing to do so at closing of the Merger as well. 

This provision also applies to the directors of the Company’s subsidiaries.  

Some merger agreements also seek resignations from officers, although this provision must be implemented carefully with regard to officers, particularly with respect to practical operational issues such as signatories to bank accounts.  Note also that removal of officers also must be accomplished in compliance with any applicable employment agreements (possibly including, particularly for foreign subsidiaries, employment terms imposed by applicable law).

The Company is not required to obtain resignations unless so requested by Parent.  For example, Parent might not be concerned if a group of the Company’s continuing employees continue to serve as directors of its subsidiaries.  In the case of foreign subsidiaries, where there is often a requirement for resident directors, leaving directors in place rather than finding new qualified directors may be the most practical course of action for Parent.  There are often statutory or regulatory requirements for the replacement of foreign corporation directors.

6.09.Ti=	Rule 16b-3.  

Prior to the Effective Time, the Company shall take all such steps as may be required to cause any dispositions of equity securities of the Company  in connection with the Contemplated Transactions (including derivative securities) by each individual who is subject to the reporting requirements of Section 16(a) of the Exchange Act with respect to the Company and will be subject to such reporting requirements with respect to Parent to be exempt under Rule 16b-3 promulgated under the Exchange Act.

COMMENT:

Under U.S. securities laws, the shares of the Company held by officers and directors of the Company who are subject to Section 16 of the Exchange Act that are exchanged for cash in the Offer or the Merger may be a disposition of their securities that could be matched against other acquisitions of Company securities within a six-month period under the Section 16 short swing profit rules promulgated under Section 16 of the Exchange Act (which under those rules could be prior to, as well as after, that disposition).  

The SEC staff provided interpretive relief against these concerns in a 1999 no-action letter (SEC letter to Skadden, Arps, Jan. 12, 1999).  That no-action letter provides that, in connection with a merger (which would include a front end tender offer pursuant to a merger agreement), the conversion of target equity securities (including derivative securities) into cash is deemed a disposition to the target (even though payment may be made by the buyer directly to target security holders) eligible for exemption under Rule 16b-3(e).

To take advantage of this exemption, specific board or compensation committee approvals are required. The SEC staff letter requires the applicable board approval be given during the period commencing with such board’s approval of the merger agreement and ending before disposition of the securities.  Such approval must contain the following:

•	The name of each officer or director;

•	The number of securities to be acquired or disposed of for each named person; and

•	That the approval is granted for purposes of exempting the transaction under Rule 16b-3.

While some parties try to take these steps relatively early in the merger process, such as at the time their respective boards approve execution of the merger agreement, it may be advisable to take these steps closer in time to the actual disposition of the Company securities, when all the information with respect to the affected individuals may be more clear.

Form 3 and Form 4 Filing Requirements.  Note that under current SEC requirements, the disposition of securities in the Offer or the Merger by the target’s directors and executive officers must be reported on Forms 4 within two business days of the disposition of Company securities.

6.10.Ti=	Rule 14d-10 Matters.  

Prior to the Acceptance Time and to the extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements, the Compensation Committee of the Company Board, at a meeting duly called and held, will approve each agreement, arrangement or understanding entered into by Purchaser, the Company or their respective Affiliates on or after the date hereof with any of the officers, directors or employees of the Company pursuant to which compensation is paid to such officer, director or employee to be approved as an "employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangement” within the meaning of Rule 14d-10(d)(2) under the Exchange Act and to take all other action reasonably necessary to satisfy the requirements of the non-exclusive safe harbor set forth in Rule 14d-10(d)(2) under the Exchange Act.

[NTD:  cross-x discussion under 3.11 and expand if necessary to deal with covenant context]

COMMENT:

As discussed in the comment to Section 3.11, Rule 14d-10, which includes the "best price rule,” provides that no bidder may make a tender offer "unless . . . the consideration paid to any security holder for securities tendered. . . is the highest consideration paid to any other security holder for securities tendered. . .”  (see Exchange Act Rule 14d-10(a)(2)).  If the Company’s officers, directors and employees are also holders of the Company’s securities and tender such securities into the tender offer, there is the concern that any severance or other employee-related payments to such officers, directors and employees in connection with the consummation of the transaction might implicate Rule 14d-10 and that Purchaser would be in violation of the best-price rule if such payments were considered payments for securities tendered.  

The 2006 amendments adopted by the SEC to the best-price rule clarify that it applies only to consideration offered and paid for tendered securities and does not apply to employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangements entered into with a target’s security holders.  Payments under employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangements are outside the scope of the rule if they are both (i) for past services performed or future services to be refrained from performing and (ii) not calculated based on the number of securities tendered (see Exchange Act Rule 14d-10(d)(1)).  

The rule includes a non-exclusive safe harbor for compensatory arrangements approved by independent directors constituting a compensation committee or another committee performing functions similar to a compensation committee (or a special committee if neither such committee exists or is independent) of a target board, regardless of whether the target is a party to such arrangements, or, if Purchaser is a party to such arrangements, of the Purchaser board (see Exchange Act Rule 14d-10(d)(2)).  Section 6.10 requires the Company Board, in accordance with the non-exclusive safe harbor offered in Rule 14d-10(d)(2), to approve agreements, arrangements or understanding entered into on or after the date of the Agreement as an "employment compensation, severance or other employee benefit arrangement” within the meaning of Rule 14d-10(d)(2).  

As drafted the covenant offers Purchaser protection against agreements, arrangements or understanding entered into after signing the Agreement, but not against those already in place and pursuant to which payments will be made in connection with the consummation of the transactions.  Accordingly, Purchaser may seek to revise the covenant to apply to agreements, arrangements or understandings that "have been or will be” entered into and pursuant to which payments are made or are to be made or benefits are granted or are to be granted.  

An alternative to expanding the scope of the covenant would be for the Company to give Purchaser a representation and warranty that  existing agreements have been approved as required to utilize the safe-harbor.  As discussed in the comment to Section 3.11, the Company would want to narrow the scope of such a representation to a specified period of time prior to the date of the Agreement, such as agreements adopted since the commencement of discussions with Purchaser, and/or a specific set of agreements, arrangements and understanding. 

Another comment that Purchaser may have in connection with this covenant is that Purchase should be given an opportunity to review and comment on drafts of the resolutions to be adopted in satisfaction of the covenant.  

6.11.Ti=	Employee Benefits.  

6.11.(1).sec=	With respect to any Benefit Plan maintained by Parent or any of its Subsidiaries (including the Company after the Acceptance Time, and the Surviving Corporation after the Effective Time) in which any director, officer or employee of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries (the "Company Employees”) will participate effective as of or after the Acceptance Time (including any Company Benefit Plan) (such plans, the "New Benefit Plans”), Parent shall, or shall cause the Company or the Surviving Corporation, as applicable, to, (i) recognize all service of the Company Employees with the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, prior to such time, for purposes of determining eligibility to participate, vesting and accrual or entitlement to benefits where length of service is relevant in any New Benefit Plan in which such Company Employees may be eligible to participate after the Acceptance Time, other than benefit accruals under a defined benefit pension plan, (ii) assume the liability for each Company Employee's accrued personal, sick or vacation time and allow such Company Employee to use such accrued personal, sick or vacation time in accordance with the practice and policies of the Company and (iii) honor any payments, charges and expenses of such Company Employee (and his or her eligible dependents) that were applied toward the deductible, out-of-pocket maximums and co-payments under a Benefit Plan in satisfying any applicable deductibles, out-of-pocket maximums and co-payments under the corresponding New Benefit Plan during the same plan year in which such payments, charges and expenses were made.

6.11.(2).sec=	From and after the Acceptance Time, the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any other Subsidiary of Parent, as applicable, shall honor, and Parent shall cause the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any other Subsidiary of Parent, as applicable, to honor, in accordance with their terms, all individual employment, deferred compensation, severance and change of control agreements, plans or policies between the Company or any of its Subsidiaries and any current or former director, officer or employee of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, including, without limitation, bonuses, incentives or deferred compensation, in existence as of the Acceptance Time.

6.11.(3).sec=	From and after the Acceptance Time, the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any other Subsidiary of Parent, as applicable, shall, and Parent shall cause the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any other Subsidiary of Parent to, provide or pay when due to any current or former director, officer or employee of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, all benefits and compensation pursuant to the Company Benefit Plans or any other compensatory programs and arrangements of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries in effect as of the Acceptance Time earned or accrued through, and to which such individuals are entitled as of, the Acceptance Time (or such later time as such benefit plans, compensatory programs and arrangements as in effect at the Acceptance Time are terminated or canceled by the Company or the Surviving Corporation, as applicable, subject to compliance with this 6.12).

6.11.(4).sec=	For a period ending two years after the Acceptance Time, the Company or the Surviving Corporation, as applicable, shall, and Parent shall cause the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any other Subsidiary of Parent, as applicable, to, provide to each of the Company Employees (i) salaries or wages that are no less than those paid to such Company Employee by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries immediately prior to the Acceptance Time, (ii) overall compensation that is at least substantially comparable to that provided to such Company Employee by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries immediately prior to the Acceptance Time, (iii) bonus opportunities that are no less favorable than those provided to such Company Employee by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries immediately prior to the Acceptance Time, and (iv) employee benefits that are no less favorable in the aggregate than those provided to such Company Employee under the Company Benefit Plans or any other compensatory programs and arrangements of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries in effect immediately prior to the Acceptance Time.

6.11.(5).sec=	Nothing in this Agreement shall require the continued employment of any Company Employee after the Acceptance Time, and, except as set forth in this Section 6.12, no provision of this Agreement shall prevent Parent or any of its Subsidiaries (including the Company after the Acceptance Time, and the Surviving Corporation after the Effective Time) from amending or terminating any Company Benefit Plan or any other compensatory program and arrangement of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries.

6.11.(6).sec=	All provisions contained in this Agreement with respect to employee benefit plans or employee compensation are included for the sole benefit of the respective Parties and shall not create any third-party beneficiary or other right in any other person, including any employee or former employee of the Company, the Surviving Corporation or any participant or beneficiary in any Company Benefit Plan.

6.12.Ti=	Indemnification of Officers and Directors.  

6.12.(1).sec=	All rights to indemnification and exculpation from liabilities for acts or omissions occurring at or prior to the Effective Time and rights to advancement of expenses relating thereto now existing in favor of any person who is or prior to the Effective Time becomes, or has been at any time prior to the date of this Agreement, a director, officer, employee or agent (including as a fiduciary with respect to an employee benefit plan) of the Company, any of its Subsidiaries or any of their respective predecessors (the "Indemnified Persons”) as provided in the Company Certificate of Incorporation, the Company By-Laws, the organizational documents of any Subsidiary of the Company or any indemnification agreement between such Indemnified Party and the Company or any of its Subsidiaries (each as in effect as of the date of this Agreement) shall survive the Merger and shall not be amended, repealed or otherwise modified in any manner that would adversely affect any right thereunder of any such Indemnified Party.

6.12.(2).sec=	Without limiting Section 6.13(a) or any rights of any Indemnified Person pursuant to any indemnification agreement, from and after the Effective Time, in the event of any threatened or actual claim, suit, action, proceeding or investigation (a "Claim”), whether civil, criminal or administrative, based in whole or in part on, or arising in whole or in part out of, or pertaining to (i) the fact that the Indemnified Person is or was a director (including in a capacity as a member of any board committee), officer, employee or agent of the Company, any of its Subsidiaries or any of their respective predecessors or (ii) this Agreement or any of the Contemplated Transactions, whether in any case asserted or arising before or after the Effective Time, Parent and the Surviving Corporation shall, jointly and severally, indemnify, defend and hold harmless, as and to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements, each such Indemnified Person against any losses, claims, damages, liabilities, costs, expenses (including reasonable attorney’s fees and expenses in advance of the final disposition of any claim, suit, proceeding or investigation to each Indemnified Person to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Legal Requirements upon receipt of any undertaking required by applicable Legal Requirements), judgments, fines and amounts paid in settlement of or in connection with any such threatened or actual Claim.  Neither Parent nor the Surviving Corporation shall settle, compromise or consent to the entry of any judgment in any threatened or actual Claim for which indemnification could be sought by an Indemnified Person hereunder, unless such settlement, compromise or consent includes an unconditional release of such Indemnified Person from all liability arising out of such Claim or such Indemnified Person otherwise consents in writing to such settlement, compromise or consent.  Parent and the Surviving Corporation shall cooperate with an Indemnified Person in the defense of any matter for which such Indemnified Person could seek indemnification hereunder.  Parent’s and the Surviving Corporation’s obligations under this Section 6.13(b) shall continue in full force and effect for a period of six years from the Effective Time; provided, hat all rights to indemnification in respect of any Claim asserted or made within such period shall continue until the final disposition of such Claim.

6.12.(3).sec=	The Company may obtain, at or prior to the Effective Time, prepaid (or "tail”) directors’ and officers’ liability insurance policies in respect of acts or omissions occurring at or prior to the Effective Time (including for acts or omissions occurring in connection with the approval of this Agreement and the consummation of the Contemplated Transactions) for six years from the Effective Time, covering each person who is covered by such policies on the date of this Agreement on terms with respect to such coverage and amounts that are, individually and in the aggregate, no less favorable to any Indemnified Party than those of such policies in effect on the date of this Agreement; provided, however, that the maximum aggregate annual premium for such insurance policies for any such year shall not exceed the maximum aggregate annual premium contemplated by the second succeeding sentence.  If such "tail” insurance policies have been obtained by the Company, Parent shall cause such policies to be maintained in full force and effect, for their full term, and cause all obligations thereunder to be honored by it and the Surviving Corporation.

If the Company does not obtain such "tail” insurance policies, then, for a period of six years from the Effective Time, Parent shall maintain in effect the Company’s current directors’ and officers’ liability insurance policies in respect of acts or omissions occurring at or prior to the Effective Time (including for acts or omissions occurring in connection with the approval of this Agreement and the consummation of the transactions contemplated hereby), covering each Indemnified Person on terms with respect to such coverage and amounts that are, individually and in the aggregate, no less favorable to any Indemnified Person than those of such policies in effect on the date of this Agreement; provided, that neither Parent nor the Surviving Corporation shall be required to pay an aggregate annual premium for such insurance policies in excess of 300% of the annual premium paid by the Company for coverage for its last full fiscal year for such insurance; provided, further, that if the annual premium of such insurance coverage exceeds such amount, Parent or the Surviving Corporation shall be obligated to obtain a policy with the greatest coverage available for a cost not exceeding such amount; and provided, further, that Parent may substitute therefor policies of a reputable and financially sound insurance company containing terms, including with respect to coverage and amounts, that are, individually and in the aggregate, no less favorable to any Indemnified Person.

6.12.(4).sec=	In the event that Parent or the Surviving Corporation or any of their respective successors or assigns (i) consolidates with or merges into any other person and is not the continuing or surviving corporation or entity of such consolidation or merger or (ii) transfers or conveys all or a substantial portion of its properties and other assets to any person, or if Parent dissolves the Surviving Corporation, then, and in each such case, Parent shall cause proper provision to be made so that the applicable successors and assigns or transferees expressly assume the obligations set forth in this Section 6.13.

6.12.(5).sec=	The obligations of Parent and the Surviving Corporation under this Section 6.13 shall not be terminated or modified in such a manner as to adversely affect any Indemnified Person to whom this Section 6.13 applies without the consent of such affected Indemnified Person.  The provisions of this Section 6.13 are intended to be for the benefit of, and will be enforceable by, each Indemnified Person, his or her heirs and his or her representatives, and are in addition to, and not in substitution for, any other rights to indemnification or contribution that any such person may have by contract or otherwise

6.12.(6).sec=	This Section 6.13 shall survive the consummation of the Merger and continue in full force and effect and is intended to benefit, and shall be enforceable by each Indemnified Person as a third party beneficiary.

COMMENT:

This section addresses indemnification after the effective date for officers, directors, employees and agents of the Company and its subsidiaries serving in such capacities prior to the Merger.  Termination of service as an officer, director, employee or agent does not result in termination of the liabilities associated with such service.  Persons potentially affected by these liabilities would be not only those officers, directors, employees or agents at the effective date, but their predecessors as well.  

Subsection (a) is intended to provide such persons with the same rights to indemnification from specified liabilities which are incurred in connection with their official capacities as exist prior to the Merger.  These rights arise out of several sources:  charter and bylaw provisions, contractual agreements, and other undertakings creating such rights. There is no expiration of the obligations on Parent specified in clause(a) with respect to the specific organizational documents and indemnification agreements, and Parent may seek to limit the applicability of the covenant to the six-year period following the closing of the merger.

Clause (b) contains a separate indemnification obligation from Parent to the covered individuals in connection with their official duties prior to the effective time and the matters leading to the execution of the Agreement and consummation of the Contemplated Transactions.
