Here the Company is seeking to provide the indemnified persons with the broadest possible indemnification, even if not provided under such persons’ current arrangements.  Such indemnification from Parent  provides broader protection to the Company directors than would be available from the Company itself, since indemnification by the Company is limited by Section 145 of the DGCL in circumstances involving, among other things, breaches of loyalty or claims by or in right of the corporation, but the indemnity by Parent would be provided by contract and so arguably not subject to such limits.  A direct undertaking from Parent also gives the indemnified persons the credit of the buyer in addition to that of the surviving corporation. 

Parent may seek to have the provision include additional detail on the indemnification procedures the covered persons must follow to avail themselves of the indemnification, such as delivering notice of the potential indemnifiable matter to Parent and allowing Parent to control the defense of the matter absence certain conflicts of interest.  In addition, Parent may seek to require the indemnified party to provide an undertaking to return any expenses advanced if it is determined that the indemnified person is determined not to be entitled to such indemnification., with such determination to be made either by independent counsel to the surviving corporation or a court of competent jurisdiction.

Subsection (c) is intended to ensure that an insurance policy is available for a certain time to protect directors and officers in the event that indemnification is not available.  Indemnification may be unavailable because (i) the contractual provisions in existence do not provide for it, (ii) it is not legally permitted or (iii) the indemnitor is insolvent.  The provisions address the concerns of the resigning executive officers and directors of the Company by requiring a policy with known coverage provisions and the concerns of Parent by limiting both the amount to be paid for such coverage and the time period during which the coverage must be maintained.

"Tail” Policies.  Historically, merger agreements have required the surviving corporation to maintain insurance covering former directors and officers during the relevant time period.  In recent years, more agreements have moved toward the purchase of a single "tail” policy.  The insurance covenant found in subsection (c) permits the Company to buy a tail policy from the Company’s existing insurer or other insurer.  A tail policy would provide coverage for a number of years after closing for acts or omissions that occurred during the period covered by the previous (pre-merger) policy.  Such a policy could provide for payment directly to the claimant rather than requiring the claimant to submit a claim through the surviving entity, eliminate the risk of non-payment of premiums, and eliminate the risk associated with applying for a new policy from a new insurer who may choose to include exclusions from coverage for certain periods, transactions, or acts.  As a practical matter, buying one multi-year tail policy also might be cheaper than the aggregate purchase price of a series of one-year insurance policies covering the same period.  

The Company and its directors will want to purchase a tail policy to avoid issues with indemnification from Parent and surviving corporation, and will want to do so prior to the Acceptance Time so as to ensure all of the directors can participate in making the determination of the tail policy to purchase.

Subsequent Corporate Events.  Clause (d) ensures that the obligations imposed on Parent in Section 6.13 will survive any future changes of control or transfers of all or substantially all of the assets of Parent by imposing a requirement that the successors of Parent assume the obligations. This provision, coupled with the third party beneficiary provision described below, is necessary to ensure the indemnified persons are able to enjoy the protections afforded by the covenant in light of subsequent corporate changes. 

Enforcement as Third Party Beneficiaries.  Because the target officers and directors are not parties to the Agreement, they need a mechanism for enforcing the provisions of this section.  Clause (e)  provides this mechanism by providing that the target officers and directors are intended to be third-party beneficiaries of, and entitled to enforce, this section.

6.13.Ti=	Purchaser Compliance.  

Parent shall cause Purchaser to comply promptly with all of Purchaser’s obligations under this Agreement and Purchaser shall not engage in any activities of any nature except as provided in or contemplated by this Agreement.

COMMENT:

The requirement that Parent cause Merger Sub to comply with the Agreement is arguably not needed as Merger Sub will be a party to the Agreement and the Company will have direct rights of enforcement against it. However, the provision recognizes that Parent is the sole stockholder of Merger Sub and can easily cause Merger Sub to comply with the Agreement, in addition to giving the Company a direct cause of action against Parent for Merger Sub’s actions.  In addition, the covenant also requires Parent to cause Merger Sub not to undertake any actions except as contemplated by the Agreement, which is intended to ensure that Merger Sub will be capable of consummating the Offer and the Merger when the conditions to each are satisfied and will have a contracts or liabilities preventing it from doing so.

6.14.Ti=	Takeover Laws; Advice of Changes.  

If any Takeover Law may become, or may purport to be, applicable to the transactions contemplated in this Agreement, each of Parent and the Company and the members of their respective boards of directors will grant such approvals and take such actions as are necessary so that the transactions contemplated by this Agreement may be consummated as promptly as practicable on the terms and conditions contemplated hereby and thereby and otherwise act to eliminate the effect of any Takeover Law on any of the transactions contemplated by this Agreement.

6.15.Ti=	Financing.



COMMENT:

Purchaser Financing Covenant



Should it be contemplated that the purchaser will obtain debt financing in connection with the transaction (typically through a debt commitment letter as discussed in the Comment to Section 4.08), the target will typically require the purchaser to covenant to use certain efforts (ideally, "reasonable best efforts”) to obtain the committed debt financing on the terms set forth in the commitment letter. The financing covenant also typically includes the purchaser’s agreement:



•	not to permit any modification of the terms of the financing commitments without the target’s consent, subject to certain limited exceptions (such as adding or replacing lenders),



•	to maintain the financing commitment letters in effect and comply with all obligations thereunder,



•	to enter into definitive agreements for the debt financing (sometimes within a specified number of days of signing the agreement); 



•	to notify the target if certain events (such as default) occur under the debt financing commitment letter, 



•	to obtain alternative financing (generally, on terms not materially less favorable to the purchaser) if the original financing contemplated by the financing commitment letters becomes unavailable. 



One component of the covenant to obtain the financing under the financing commitment letters is that the buyer generally agrees to use reasonable efforts (or a similar standard) to enforce its rights under the commitment letters



The following is an example of a financing covenant that could be proposed by the target:

"Financing.

6.15.(1).sec=	Upon the terms and subject to conditions of this Agreement, each of Parent and Purchaser shall use its reasonable best efforts to take or cause to be taken all actions, and to do or cause to be done, all things necessary or advisable to obtain the Financing on the terms and conditions (including the flex provisions) described in the Commitment Letter, and shall not permit any amendment or modification to be made to, or any waiver of any provision under, the Commitment Letter if such amendment, modification or waiver 

(x) reduces (or could have the effect of reducing) the aggregate amount of the Financing (including by increasing the amount of fees to be paid or original issue discount unless the Financing is increased by a corresponding amount or the Financing is otherwise made available to fund such fees or original issue discount), 

(y) imposes new or additional conditions or otherwise expands, amends or modifies any of the conditions to the Financing, or otherwise expands, amends or modifies any other provision of the Commitment Letter, in a manner materially adverse to Parent, Purchaser or the Company or 

(z) otherwise be reasonably likely to (i) prevent or materially adversely affect the ability of Parent to fund its obligations at the Offer Acceptance Time and the Closing Date or (ii) materially adversely impact the ability of Parent, Merger Sub or the Company to enforce its rights against the other parties to the Commitment Letter or the definitive agreements with respect thereto. 

Parent shall promptly deliver to the Company copies of any such amendment, modification or replacement.  For purposes of this Section 6.15, references to "Financing” shall include the financing contemplated by the Commitment Letter as permitted to be amended, modified or replaced by this Section 6.15(a) and references to "Commitment Letter” shall include such documents as permitted to be amended, modified or replaced by this Section 6.15(a). 

6.15.(2).sec=	Each of Parent and Purchaser shall use its reasonable best efforts to 

(i)	maintain in effect the Commitment Letter, 

(ii)	negotiate and enter into definitive agreements with respect to the Commitment Letter on the terms and conditions (including the flex provisions) contained in the Commitment Letter (or on other terms not materially less favorable to Parent or Purchaser and that do not materially impair the ability of Parent and Purchaser to fund their obligations at the Offer Acceptance Time and the Closing Date), 

(iii)	satisfy on a timely basis all conditions to funding in the Commitment Letter and such definitive agreements thereto and to consummate the Financing at or prior to the Offer acceptance time and the Closing Date, as applicable, including using its reasonable best efforts to cause the lenders and the other persons committing to fund the Financing at the Offer acceptance time and on the Closing, as applicable (the "Financing Sources”), 

(iv)	enforce its rights under the Commitment Letter and such definitive agreements in the event of a breach by the Financing Sources, including by seeking specific performance of the parties thereunder if necessary, and 

(v)	comply with its obligations under the Commitment Letter. 

Parent shall keep the Company reasonably informed of the status of its efforts to arrange the Financing and provide to the Company copies of the executed material definitive agreements for the Financing. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, Parent and Purchaser shall give the Company prompt notice:

(w)	of any material breach or material default by any party to any of the Commitment Letter or definitive agreements related to the Financing of which Parent or Purchaser become aware, 

(x)	of the receipt of (A) any written notice or (B) other written communication, in each case, from any Financing Source with respect to any actual or potential breach, default, termination or repudiation by any party to any of the Commitment Letter or definitive agreements related to the Financing of any provisions of the Commitment Letter or definitive agreements related to the Financing,

(y)	of any material dispute or disagreement between or among any parties to the Commitment Letter or any such definitive agreement related to the Financing that would reasonably be expected to materially hinder or delay the consummation of the Contemplated Transactions and 

(z)	if at any time for any reason Parent or Purchaser believes in good faith that it will not be able to obtain all or any portion of the Financing on the terms and conditions, in the manner or from the Financing Sources contemplated by any of the Commitment Letter or definitive agreements related to the Financing. 

As soon as reasonably practicable, but in any event within two (2) business days of the date the Company delivers to Parent or Purchaser a written request, Parent and Purchaser shall provide any information reasonably requested by the Company relating to any circumstance referred to in clause (w), (x), (y) or (z) of the immediately preceding sentence; provided, that Parent and Purchaser need not provide any information believed to be privileged.  

If any portion of the Financing becomes unavailable on the terms and conditions contemplated by the Commitment Letter, Parent and Purchaser shall use their reasonable best efforts to arrange and obtain in replacement thereof, and to negotiate and enter into definitive agreements with respect to, alternative financing from alternative sources in an amount sufficient to fund consummation of the Contemplated Transactions with terms and conditions not materially less favorable to Parent and Purchaser (or their Affiliates) than the terms and conditions set forth in the Commitment Letter as promptly as reasonably practicable following the occurrence of such event but no later than the Offer closing date.  

Parent shall deliver to the Company true and complete copies of all agreements, arrangements or understandings (including and side letters or (subject to customary redactions) fee letters) pursuant to which any such alternative source shall have committed to provide any portion of the Financing. ”

Company Financing Covenant

If the purchaser is a financial sponsor, the target’s business may be the sole or primary source of recourse for the acquisition lenders.  Even if the purchaser is a strategic the target’s business will likely provide part of the credit support for any acquisition financing.  Accordingly the purchaser will require, and it is market norm for the target to provide, a covenant from the target that it will cooperate with the purchaser in obtaining the debt financing contemplated by the debt financing commitment letter.  Post-financial crisis, purchasers are requiring more detailed and extensive requirements for the target’s assistance with the financing, driven in large part by the lenders’ insistence on detailed syndication conditions and covenants in the debt financing commitment letters.  

The target’s cooperation covenant obliges the target to use its commercially reasonable efforts to assist with the Financing, and to undertake certain specific undertakings to support this general assistance obligation. The list of specific target undertakings often includes the target’s agreement to use "reasonable best” efforts (or "commercially reasonable” efforts, or a similar formulation) to: 

•	participate in lender meetings, rating agency presentations, and bond offering road shows, and prepare related documents (bank book, rating agency presentation, and bond offering documents); 



•	execute definitive loan documents and certificates (including a solvency certificate) for closing of the financing; and 



•	obtain auditor comfort letters and legal opinions. 



The financing cooperation covenant will usually include an obligation of the target to deliver "Required Information” to start the "Marketing Period” (which is a minimum number of days that must elapse before the Offer closing to allow for the marketing of the purchaser’s financing.  These two definitions are often the most heavily negotiated of the financing-related provisions in the tender/merger agreement. In general, "Required Information” is the financial information needed by the purchaser to prepare an offering document for its debt financing. There is an important distinction between "Required Information” (which must be provided before the closing of the acquisition) and the other information and assistance required by the cooperation covenant (which usually requires only "commercially reasonable efforts” or similar standard to satisfy). For this reason, the target will want to move as many requirements as possible out of the "Required Information” definition and into the general provisions of the financing assistance covenant.



The target usually requires the purchaser to indemnify the target for any actions taken in connection with the financing and to reimburse the target for any fees and expenses that it incurs by its compliance with the cooperation covenant. The covenant also customarily makes clear that the target will not be liable for any fees or expenses related to the financing unless and until the acquisition closes. 



The following is an example of a financing assistance covenant that could be proposed by the target:

6.15.(3).sec=	"Financing Assistance.  Prior to the Effective Time, the Company shall, and shall cause its Subsidiaries to, at Parent’s sole expense, use their respective commercially reasonable efforts to cooperate with Parent in connection with the Financing or any permitted replacement, amended, modified or alternative financing ("Available Financing”) (provided that such requested cooperation does not unreasonably interfere with the ongoing operations of the Company and its Subsidiaries in any material respect). Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, upon reasonable request by Parent, the Company shall, and shall cause its Subsidiaries to, use their respective commercially reasonable efforts to:

6.15.(3).(1).sec=	(i)	the extent reasonably necessary in connection with the Financing, make senior officers of the Company available to attend reasonable number of meetings (A) with prospective lenders, investors and ratings agencies, (B) in connection with a "roadshow”, (C) in connection with customary due diligence sessions and drafting sessions and sessions with ratings agencies, at such times as coordinated reasonably in advance thereof, 

6.15.(3).(2).sec=	(ii)	assist Parent with the preparation of customary materials for rating agency presentations, road-show presentations, offering documents, private placement memoranda, bank information memoranda and similar documents (to the extent such customary materials contain disclosure reflecting or referring to the Company and its Subsidiaries) reasonably necessary or advisable in connection with the Financing, 

6.15.(3).(3).sec=	(iii)	furnish in a timely fashion the Company’s most recently completed audited financial statements, the Company’s interim financial statements for the Company’s current fiscal year and all other information regarding the Company and its Subsidiaries reasonably required for the Parent to prepare pro forma financial statements and other pro forma financial data that would be customarily included in bank information memoranda for the syndication of term loan and bridge loan commitments contemplated under the Commitment Letter (collectively, the "Required Information”); provided, that with respect to the foregoing clauses (A) through (C), no such financial statements or other information are required to be provided with respect to any of the Company or its Subsidiaries on an unconsolidated basis; 

6.15.(3).(4).sec=	(iv)	assist with the preparation of definitive financing documents and provide the financial institutions that have committed to provide the Financing (the "Financing Sources”) with reasonable access to the properties, books and records of the Company and its Subsidiaries during normal working hours (to the extent practicable) and upon reasonable notice, 

6.15.(3).(5).sec=	(v)	cause its independent registered public accounting firm to (A) consent to SEC filings and offering memoranda that include or incorporate the Company’s consolidated financial information and their reports thereon, in each case, to the extent such consent is required, (B) deliver to Parent and Parent’s board of directors and any underwriter of the Financing a customary auditor "comfort letter” to the extent such Financing constitutes a registered or 144A offering of debt securities, (C) reasonable assistance in the preparation of pro forma financial statements by the Parent and (D) provide reasonable assistance and cooperation to Parent, including attending customary accounting due diligence sessions, 

6.15.(3).(6).sec=	(vi)	only to the extent required in connection with the Financing, to permit Parent to display the logos of the Company in a format approved by the Company in materials distributed in connection with the Financing, provided, that Parent and its Affiliates comply with all reasonable instructions of the Company with respect to such display and ceases any and all such use by the Effective Time or the date of termination of this Agreement, 

6.15.(3).(7).sec=	(vii) 	reasonably cooperate with the Parent and the Financing Source or any of their respective agents and counsel with respect to their due diligence, including by giving access to documentation reasonably and customarily requested by persons in connection with capital markets transactions, and 

6.15.(3).(8).sec=	(viii)	provide reasonable assistance in the preparation of and executing and delivering (or using commercially reasonable efforts to obtain from its advisors), and causing its Subsidiaries to execute and deliver (or use commercially reasonable efforts to obtain from their advisors), customary certificates, legal opinions and other documents and instruments relating to the Financing as may be reasonably requested by Parent as necessary and customary in connection with the Financing; 

provided, that the actions contemplated in the first sentence of this Section 6.15(c) and the foregoing clauses (a) through (i) do not (A) unreasonably interfere with the operations of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, (B) require the Company or any of its Subsidiaries to pay any out-of-pocket fees or expenses prior to Closing Date that are not promptly reimbursed by Parent, or (C) require the Company or any of its Subsidiaries to incur any other liability or obligation in connection with the Financing or otherwise. 

6.15.(4).sec=	Parent shall promptly, upon request by the Company, reimburse the Company for all reasonable out-of-pocket costs and expenses (including reasonable attorneys’ fees) incurred by the Company or any of its Subsidiaries in connection with the cooperation of the Company and its Subsidiaries contemplated by this Section 6.15 (including expenses associated with attending meetings, presentations, road shows and due diligence presentations).  Parent and its Affiliates shall indemnify and hold harmless the Company and its Subsidiaries and their respective officers, directors, employees, agents, Affiliates, and representatives (collectively, the "Financing Indemnitees”) from and against any and all losses, damages, claims, costs or expenses suffered or incurred by them in connection with the arrangement of the Available Financing and any information utilized in connection therewith (other than information provided by the Company and its Subsidiaries).  The immediately preceding sentences of this Section 6.15(d) shall survive the consummation of the Merger and any termination of this Agreement, and is intended to benefit, and may be enforced by, the Financing Indemnitees and their respective Affiliates.  Section 6.15(d) may not be amended, altered or repealed after the Offer closing without the prior written consent of the affected Financing Indemnitee. 

ARTICLE 7

CONDITIONS PRECEDENT TO MERGER

7.01.Ti=	Conditions to Each Party’s Obligation to Effect the Merger.  

The respective obligation of each party hereto to effect the Merger is subject to the satisfaction or waiver on or prior to the Closing Date of the following conditions:

7.01.(1).sec=	Purchase of the Company Common Stock in the Offer.  Purchaser shall have previously accepted for payment all shares of the Company Common Stock validly tendered and not withdrawn pursuant to the Offer.   

7.01.(2).sec=	No Injunctions or Restraints.  No Order or other Law preventing the consummation of the Merger issued or promulgated by any Governmental Body of competent jurisdiction [NTD:  may want to limit to jurisdictions where the violation would have a material effect, or perhaps note this in commentary] shall be in effect; provided, that prior to asserting this condition, each of the parties hereto shall have complied with Section 6.05.

COMMENT:

Unlike a merger agreement, Article VII contains few conditions.  As this is a two-step transaction, the more meaningful conditions precedent to the consummation of the transaction are the conditions to the buyer’s obligation to close the Offer, contained in Annex A.  Once the Offer has been completed, Purchaser and, indirectly, Parent, will own a majority interest in the Company, the Merger will take place, barring extreme circumstances.  

As a process matter the Company stockholders may need to approve the Merger if either Section 251(h) were inapplicable or Purchaser cannot complete the Merger through a short-form merger, but since Purchaser owns a majority of the outstanding shares as obtained in the Offer, and has agreed to vote all such shares in favor of the Merger if a stockholder vote is required (see Section 6.04(b)), the outcome of the stockholder vote is not in question.  If Section 251(h) were inapplicable, consider replacing condition (a) with the following:  "If required by Law [NTD: "Law” is not defined ("Legal Requirement” is) but seems most used throughout, so I’m leaving this as "Law” expecting that someone will choose which to use and conform throughout], the Company shall have obtained the affirmative vote of the holders of a sufficient number of outstanding shares of the Company’s capital stock to approve this Agreement, the Merger and the other transactions contemplated hereby under the Company’s Organizational Documents and the DGCL.”

ARTICLE 8

TERMINATION, AMENDMENT AND WAIVER

COMMENT:

Article VIII sets out the circumstances under which the Agreement may be terminated.  A termination section serves a number of purposes:

•	A termination section provides assurance to the parties that their obligations under the agreement will not be open-ended if the transaction is not consummated by an outside date, commonly referred to as a "drop dead” date.

•	In the event that it becomes clear that the transaction cannot be consummated, for example as a result of the failure of the tender offer to attract sufficient shares or the entry of a final order by a regulatory body prohibiting the transaction, the termination section will permit a party to terminate the agreement prior to the drop dead date.

•	A target will seek to negotiate provisions in the termination section to preserve flexibility for the target board to comply with its fiduciary duties.  [NTD:  Seems strong if termination right not actually required by fiduciary duties.]

•	The termination section may provide for a termination fee and/or in some instances expense reimbursement in connection with or as a result of certain terminations.

•	The termination section identifies provisions of the agreement that will survive termination of the agreement and provides that a termination will not relieve a party of certain liabilities.

As noted in more detail in the commentary to Article 7 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement, when negotiating and drafting the termination section, counsel should be aware of the interaction between that section and the provisions relating to covenants and closing conditions (in the case of the Model Agreement both for the Offer and the Merger).

In general, these termination rights are exercisable by Parent and the Company, and only require Purchaser to join in the instance of mutual consent where all the Parties are essentially amending the agreement,  consistent with the requirements of Section 9.05(a) of the Model Agreement that all Parties join in such amendment. 

8.01.Ti=	Termination.  

This Agreement may be terminated and the Offer and the Merger may be abandoned (with respect to Sections 8.01(b) through 8.01(i), by written notice by the terminating Party to the other Party):

8.01.(1).sec=	by mutual written consent of Parent, [Purchaser] and the Company, at any time prior to the Acceptance Time;

8.01.(2).sec=	by either Parent or the Company at any time prior to the Acceptance Time and after  [__________] (the "Outside Date”) if the Acceptance Time shall not have occurred on or before the Outside Date, provided, that the right to terminate this Agreement pursuant to this Section 8.01(b) shall not be available to any Party whose failure to fulfill any obligation [material]3 breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement has caused or resulted in the failure of the Acceptance Time to occur on or before the Outside Date;

8.01.(3).sec=	by either Parent or the Company at any time prior to the Acceptance Time if a Governmental Body of competent jurisdiction shall have issued a nonappealable final order, decree or ruling or taken any other nonappealable final action, in each case having the effect of permanently restraining, enjoining or otherwise prohibiting the acceptance for payment of, and payment for, shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer or consummation of the Merger; provided, that a Party shall not be permitted to terminate this Agreement pursuant to this Section 8.01(c) if a [material]4 breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement by such Party (or any Affiliate of such Party) has caused or resulted in the issuance of any such order, decree, ruling or other action;

8.01.(4).sec=	by Parent or the Company if the Offer (as it may have been extended pursuant to Section 1.01(d)) expires as a result of the non-satisfaction of the Minimum Condition, without Purchaser having accepted for payment any shares of Company Common Stock validly tendered (and not validly withdrawn) pursuant to the Offer; provided, that a Party hereto shall not be permitted to terminate this Agreement pursuant to this Section 8.01(d) if a [material]5 breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement by such Party (or any Affiliate of such Party) has caused or resulted in the non-satisfaction of the Minimum Condition;

8.01.(5).sec=	by Parent, prior to the acceptance for payment of any shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer, if:  

8.01.(5).(1).sec=	(i)	the Company Board shall have failed to recommend the tender of shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer in the Schedule 14D-9 [or approval of the Merger or adoption of this Agreement in the Proxy Statement] or shall have effected a Change in Recommendation; 

8.01.(5).(2).sec=	(ii)	the Company Board shall have adopted, approved or recommended any Acquisition Proposal (other than the Offer and the Merger); or 

8.01.(5).(3).sec=	(iii)	a tender offer or exchange offer for outstanding shares of Company Common Stock shall have been commenced (other than by the Parent or an Affiliate of Parent) and the Company Board shall have recommended that the stockholders of the Company tender their shares in such tender or exchange offer or, within 10 business days after the commencement of such tender or exchange offer, the Company Board shall have failed to recommend against acceptance of such offer 

(each of clauses (i) through (iii), a "Trigger Event”); provided, that any such termination must occur within five (5) business days of the Trigger Event;

8.01.(6).sec=	by the Company at any time prior to the Acceptance Time, in the event that (i) in response to a Superior Proposal, the Company Board shall have effected a Change in Recommendation in accordance with Section 5.02(b), and (ii) concurrently with the termination of this Agreement, the Company pays Parent the Termination Fee contemplated by Section 8.03(a) and enters into the definitive agreement to consummate the transaction contemplated by such Superior Proposal;

8.01.(7).sec=	by Parent, prior to the acceptance for payment of any shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer, if there has been a breach of or failure to perform any representation, warranty, covenant or agreement on the part of the Company set forth in this Agreement, which breach or failure to perform (i) would cause the conditions set forth in clauses (b) or (c) of Annex I not to be satisfied, and (ii) shall not have been cured within 20 business days following receipt by the Company of written notice of such breach or failure to perform from the Parent; provided that neither Parent nor Purchaser is then in [material]6 breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement;

8.01.(8).sec=	by the Company, prior to the acceptance for payment of any shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer, if there has been a breach of or failure to perform any representation, warranty, covenant or agreement on the part of Parent or Purchaser set forth in this Agreement, which breach or failure to perform shall have had or is reasonably likely to have, individually or in the aggregate, a Parent Material Adverse Effect and shall not have been cured within 20 business days following receipt by Parent of written notice of such breach or failure to perform from the Company; provided that the Company is not then in [material]7 breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement; or

8.01.(9).sec=	by the Company (A) if, for any reason, Purchaser shall have failed to commence the Offer by the date that is 10 business days after the date of this Agreement or (B) upon two (2) business days notice to Parent, if, for any reason, Purchaser shall have failed to [purchase] all shares of Company Common Stock validly tendered (and not validly withdrawn) as of the expiration of the Offer (as it may be extended).  [NTD:  Distinguish "purchase” from occurrence of Acceptance Time, etc.]

COMMENT:

Timing of Termination.  If the Offer closes and Purchaser acquires a majority of the Company shares, it is in the mutual interest of the Parent and the Company shareholders for the Merger to be consummated as quickly as possible (for the Parent to eliminate concerns of dealing with minority holders and for the Company shareholders to receive the agreed upon consideration for their shares rather than being locked into a minority position) and all Parties should be committed to making that occur.  Thus, the termination rights under the Model Agreement are available only prior to the consummation of the Offer.  [For the same reason, the agreement provides for only limited conditions to the closing of the merger, as opposed to the conditions to the closing of the offer.  See Article VII and Annex A.]

The Model Agreement uses two different formulations for consummation of the Offer:  

•	The Acceptance Time, defined in Section 1.04(a) as the time upon which Purchaser has both accepted for payment, and paid for, shares of Company stock tendered into the Offer, is the end time for termination rights that are mutual or at the Company’s election.  [NTD:  Distinguish (h)?]

•	The acceptance for payment of shares in the Offer, without regard to the time of payment, is the end time for termination rights that are available only to Parent.  

[NTD:  Describe when/how shares are "paid for” in a tender offer.]

Although Purchaser is obligated under the securities laws to promptly pay for shares accepted for payment, there is at least a theoretical risk that such payment will not in fact be made.  Therefore, termination rights accorded exclusively to Parent eliminate any such risk (or potential out for Parent if it cannot pay) by being exercisable only prior to acceptance for payment, while mutual rights or those accorded exclusively to the Company may be exercised until payment is actually made.

Bases for Termination.  In light of the consequences tied to the termination rights, it is important to understand the bases for termination, each of which is discussed below.

Mutual Consent.  Pursuant to Section 8.01(a), at any time prior to the Acceptance Time, all of the Parties may jointly agree to terminate the agreement. 

"Drop Dead” Date.  Section 8.01(b) sets a date beyond which either Parent or the Company may call off the deal.  This provision is not intended to establish a target for the closing date; rather, it is designed to provide an outside date beyond which a further investment of the Parties’ resources, and the distractions and uncertainties arising from a significant transaction, may not be justified without a renegotiation of the terms of the transaction.

See the commentary to Article 7 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement for a discussion of the factors to consider in determining a drop dead date and the potential alternative provisions to extend this date if required to obtain regulatory approvals.  [NTD:  Note potential difference in timing between tender and merger, if not delayed for regulatory or other reasons]

The Model Agreement provides that the right to terminate on or after the drop dead date is not available to a Party whose material breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement has caused or resulted in the failure of the Acceptance Time to occur.  [NTD:  Add example, e.g., Purchaser’s failure of HOHW]  See the discussion below under "Limitation on Termination Right.”  If a Party willfully breaches its obligations, however, Section 8.02 preserves the rights of the Party who has performed to pursue remedies for breach in the event the agreement is terminated.  [NTD:  Discuss use of "principal cause” formulation rather than just "cause”]

Court or Government Action Blocking the Merger.  The basis for termination provided in Section  8.01(c) arises when a court of competent jurisdiction or other governmental body has taken an action that effectively blocks, or a legal requirement exists that precludes the consummation of, the Offer or the Merger. Similar to Section 8.01(a), this provision does not permit a Party to terminate if its (or its Affiliates) material breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement has caused or resulted in the taking of such action or issuance of such order.  See the discussion below under "Limitation on Termination Right.”  

See the commentary to Article 7 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement for a discussion of whether this termination right should be limited to specified courts or governmental bodies.

Failure of the Offer to Satisfy the Minimum Condition.  If insufficient shares have been tendered into the Offer as of the expiration date (as it may be extended), Section 8.01(d) permits either Parent or the Company to terminate the agreement.  This is the equivalent of a termination right in the context of a one-step merger transaction when the stockholders of the target fail to approve the transaction at a stockholder meeting called for that purpose.  Accordingly, this termination right relates solely to the failure to meet the Minimum Condition, and not any other condition to the Offer.  If some other condition to the Offer is not met, it could give rise to a termination right under another provision of Section 8.01.  Since Purchaser is required under Section 1.01(d) to extend the Offer until the Outside Date if any condition is not met upon any earlier scheduled expiration, it will likely be the case that Sections 8.01(b) and (d) will have the same practical effect.  However, if the obligations to extend the offer in Section 1.01(d) did not run to the Outside Date then these termination provisions will differ in application.

The right to terminate under Section 8.01(d) is not available to a Party if a material breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under this Agreement by such Party (or any Affiliate of such Party) has caused or resulted in the non-satisfaction of the Minimum Condition.  See the discussion below under "Limitation on Termination Right.”  

Failure to Make or Change in Recommendation, Approval of Alternative Transaction or Failure to Recommend Against Competing Offer.  The termination rights in Section 8.01(e) are available only to Parent and are based upon the Company Board taking, or failing to take, specified actions that may indicate that it no longer supports or is reconsidering its support of the transaction.  These include the failure to recommend in favor of the Offer and the Merger, any change in such recommendation, approval or recommendation of any other acquisition transaction, or the failure to recommend against any competing tender offer within 10 business days.  The last action resulting in a termination right is based upon Rule 14e-2, which requires a target board to make a recommendation with respect to a tender offer within 10 business days of the commencement of such offer.   

Section 8.01(e) requires that this termination right must be exercised, if at all, within five business days of the action or failure to act resulting in the termination right.  Parent may object to the requirement to exercise its termination right within this short window period.

When considering the implications of this basis for termination, one should also carefully review Section 5.02 (and, more specifically, the definition of "Change in Recommendation”).  The termination rights given to the acquirer as a result of actions or inactions of the target board in Section 7.1(e) of the ABA Model Merger Agreement are much broader; see Section 7.1(e) and the related commentary for a discussion of alternatives that Parent and the Company may seek to negotiate.

Fiduciary Termination Right.  As a seller favorable draft, the Model Agreement includes a fiduciary termination right in Section 8.01(f) pursuant to which the Company may terminate the agreement to enter into an alternate agreement to consummate a more favorable transaction, provided that it pays to Parent the termination fee set forth in Section 8.03.

While the Company Board must be free to meet its disclosure obligations under securities laws, including Rules 14d-9 and 14e-2, and Delaware law, such obligations do not require that the Company have the right to terminate the agreement and enter into a transaction that the Company Board has determined is more favorable.  See the commentary to Section 7.1(i) of the ABA Model Merger Agreement for a discussion of the alternatives to the termination right in Section 8.01(f), as well as positions that Parent and the Company may assert in negotiating this termination right. [NTD: Should commentary be expanded and go into more detail about requirements and possible issues?] 

Inaccurate Representations/Warranties or Breaches of Covenants by the Company.  The basis for termination provided in Section 8.01(g) is available only to Parent.  It arises in the event of inaccuracies in the Company’s representations and warranties and in the event of breaches of the Company’s covenants that, in either case, excuse consummation of the Offer for failure to meet the conditions in clauses (b) or (c) of Annex I to the Model Agreement, and are not cured within 20 business days after written notice of such inaccuracy or breach has been provided to the Company.  A materiality limitation on this right is introduced by the references to clauses (b) and (c) of Annex I, which include materiality qualifications for both such inaccuracies and breaches.  The cure period is also favorable to the Company, requiring written notice before the period commences and the cure period must run even if the inaccuracy or breach is not curable.  In addition, the termination right is subject to the further limitation that Parent is not then in material breach of any representation, warranty or covenant.  See the discussion below under "Limitation on Termination Right.”  

See Section 7.1(f) of the ABA Model Merger Agreement for a termination provision in the context of a one-step merger that is much more favorable to the acquirer, as well as commentary discussing alternatives that Parent and the Company may seek to negotiate.

Inaccurate Representations/Warranties or Breaches of Covenants by Parent.  Section 8.01(h) provides the Company a reciprocal right to terminate as granted to Parent under Section 8.01(g), except the breach by Parent is tied to the interference with or delay in consummating the transaction or compliance with Parent’s obligations under the agreement rather than the closing conditions of the Offer and has a prospective element ("shall have had or is reasonably likely to have”).  The cure period and absence of breach by the terminating Party are the same as in Section 8.01(g).

Failure to Commence or Consummate Offer. Section 8.01(i) provides the Company the right to terminate if Purchaser shall have failed to commence the Offer or shall have failed to purchase shares validly tendered upon the expiration of the Offer.   As a seller friendly draft this termination right does not include any limitation upon the exercise of this right if the Company’s breach contributed to such failure.  

Parent may also seek to clarify that clause (B) would not apply if Purchaser’s failure to purchase is the result of one or more conditions to the Offer set forth in Annex I not being satisfied as of the expiration of the Offer.  [While the requirement in Section 1.01(d) of the Model Agreement that the Offer be extended until the Outside Date in the event all conditions are not met or waived means that either party could also terminate under Section 8.01(b) in such event, a different extension provision in Section 1.01(d) would make such a change more meaningful.]

Limitation on Termination Right.  The termination rights in Sections 8.01(b), (c), (d), (g) and (h) each require that the terminating Party (and in certain cases its Affiliates as well) not be in material breach of any representation, warranty or covenant under the agreement in order to exercise the termination right.  In many instances where a termination of an agreement may be threatened, disputes may arise regarding possible breaches of the agreement by the terminating party that caused or contributed to the circumstances giving rise to the termination right.  As a seller friendly draft, this limitation is included in most of the termination rights on the theory that more of the termination rights are in favor of Parent and more often Parent will be seeking to assert termination rights even where the right is mutual.  It is not included in Sections 8.01(e), (f) or (i) since these provisions involve more specific actions or inactions that are specifically required or permitted under the Model Agreement where the conduct of the terminating Party is likely irrelevant, although as noted above Purchaser could seek to incorporate this concept into Section 8.01(i).

Conceptually, this limitation should be applied in a uniform manner, although the parties could seek to distinguish among the provisions.  The seller may prefer to delete the materiality qualifier in this limitation, especially where the seller is concerned that the acquirer may be much more likely to seek to terminate the deal as a business matter than the seller.  For the same reason the acquirer may seek to include a materiality qualifier and/or to include some additional qualification such as that the breach was the ‘primary’ or ‘principal’ reason that the circumstances triggering the termination right arose.  

8.02.Ti=	Effect of Termination.  

In the event of the termination of this Agreement as provided in Section 8.01, this Agreement shall be of no further force or effect; provided, that this Section 8.02, Section 8.03 and Article IX [other?] shall survive the termination of this Agreement and shall remain in full force and effect; and provided, further, that the termination of this Agreement shall not relieve any Party from any liability for fraud or willful breach.  [NTD:  Do we want to add a definition of willful breach to the Model Agreement?  NTD:  YES, AND ADD COMMENTARY AS TO COURT VIEWS, E.G. GUIDANT]]

COMMENT:

Section 8.02 provides that termination of the agreement does not affect the negotiated rights and obligations of the Parties under Section 8.03 relating to expense reimbursement and termination fees [or other provisions that the Parties have agreed will survive such termination].  

Section 8.02 also provides that termination will not relieve a Party from any liability for fraud or willful breach of the agreement.  In other words, even if the agreement is terminated under circumstances in which an expense reimbursement or termination fee payment obligation of the Company is triggered, the payment of these amounts will not release the Company from liability to Parent for any additional loss or damage that it has suffered, if the loss or damage results from the Company’s fraud or willful breach.  

[NTD:  Note need for provision to avoid extinguishing breach claims if one party terminates; also, note impact on determination of other damages if termination fee/expense reimbursement provided separately; and relationship to pursuit of specific performance of the agreement] 

See the commentary to Section 7.2 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement for a discussion of the various interpretations a court may give to "willful” and for alternatives that Parent and the Company may seek to negotiate.

8.03.Ti=	Expenses; Termination Fees.  

8.03.(1).sec=	Except as set forth in this Section 8.03, all fees and expenses incurred in connection with this Agreement and the transactions contemplated by this Agreement shall be paid by the Party incurring such expenses, whether or not the Merger is consummated; provided, that the Company agrees to pay Parent (or its designees) an amount equal to $_________ (the "Termination Fee”) if this Agreement is terminated:

8.03.(1).(1).sec=	by Parent pursuant to Section 8.01(e); or

8.03.(1).(2).sec=	by the Company pursuant to Section 8.01(f).

8.03.(2).sec=	Any Termination Fee required to be paid pursuant to Section 8.03(a) shall be paid within two business days after termination by Parent or the Company, as the case may be.

COMMENT:

A provision for the payment of fees (and for reimbursement of expenses) is a common provision in acquisition transactions involving public companies.  As a seller friendly draft, the Model Agreement provides only for the payment of a termination fee, and not for any expense reimbursement.  In addition, the termination fee is payable only upon the Company Board taking an action, or failing to take an action, that triggers a termination right in favor of Parent under Section 8.01(e) or if the Company terminates under Section 8.01(f) to enter into an agreement to consummate an alternative transaction. 

See Section 7.3 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement and the related commentary for alternative termination fee and expense reimbursement provisions, as well as a discussion regarding considerations relating to the size and computation of such amounts.  In particular, Parent may seek a termination fee in the event the agreement is terminated under Sections 8.01(b) or (g) and within a specified period of time the Company consummates an alternative acquisition transaction with a third party.

Timing of Payments.  The timing of the reimbursement and termination fee payments is addressed in Section 8.03(b).  The agreement provides that the Company must pay the termination fee within two business days of termination. 

Parent may seek to require that the Company pay any fee triggered by the Company terminating under Section 8.01(f) as a prerequisite to the termination; that is, the fee must be paid at the time of termination rather than two days thereafter.

ARTICLE 9

GENERAL PROVISIONS

9.01.Ti=	Amendment.  

Except as specified otherwise herein, this Agreement may be amended at any time prior to the Effective Time by the Parties (by action taken or authorized by their respective boards of directors, in the case of the Company and Purchaser), whether before or after adoption of this Agreement by the stockholders of the Company or Purchaser; provided, that after any such stockholder approval of this Agreement, no amendment shall be made to this Agreement that by law requires further approval or authorization by the stockholders of the Company or Purchaser without such further approval or authorization.  This Agreement may not be amended, except by an instrument in writing signed by or on behalf of each of the Parties.

9.02.Ti=	Remedies Cumulative; Waiver.  

9.02.(1).sec=	The rights and remedies of the Parties are cumulative and not alternative.  Neither any failure nor any delay by any Party in exercising any right, power or privilege under this Agreement or any of the documents referred to in this Agreement will operate as a waiver of such right, power or privilege and no single or partial exercise of any such right, power or privilege will preclude any other or further exercise of such right, power or privilege or the exercise of any other right, power or privilege.  To the maximum extent permitted by applicable law, (i) no waiver that may be given by a Party will be applicable except in the specific instance for which it is given; and (ii) no notice to or demand on one Party will be deemed to be a waiver of any obligation of that Party or of the right of the Party giving such notice or demand to take further action without notice or demand as provided in this Agreement or the documents referred to in this Agreement.

9.02.(2).sec=	At any time prior to the Effective Time, Parent (with respect to the Company) and the Company (with respect to Parent and Purchaser, and subject to Section 1.04(c)), may, to the extent legally allowed, (i) extend the time for the performance of any of the obligations or other acts of such Party, (ii) waive any inaccuracies in the representations and warranties contained in this Agreement or any document delivered pursuant to this Agreement and (iii) waive compliance with any covenants, obligations or conditions contained in this Agreement.  Any agreement on the part of a Party to any such extension or waiver shall be valid only if set forth in a written instrument signed on behalf of such Party.

9.03.Ti=	No Survival.  

None of the representations and warranties contained in this Agreement, or any covenant in this Agreement other than Section 6.14, shall survive the Effective Time.

9.04.Ti=	Entire Agreement.  

This Agreement, including the schedules, exhibits, and amendments hereto, and the Confidentiality Agreement constitute the entire agreement among the Parties and supersede all other prior or contemporaneous agreements and understandings, both written and oral, among or between any of the Parties with respect to the subject matter hereof and thereof.

9.05.Ti=	Execution of Agreement; Counterparts; Electronic Signatures.  

9.05.(1).sec=	The Agreement may be executed in several counterparts, each of which shall be deemed an original and all of which shall constitute one and the same instrument and shall become effective when counterparts have been signed by each of the Parties and delivered to the other Parties; it being understood that all Parties need not sign the same counterpart.

9.05.(2).sec=	The exchange of signed copies of this Agreement or of any other document contemplated by this Agreement (including any amendment or any other change thereto) by any electronic means intended to preserve the original graphic and pictorial appearance of a document shall constitute effective execution and delivery of this Agreement as to the Parties and may be used in lieu of an original Agreement or other document for all purposes.  Signatures of the Parties transmitted by any electronic means referenced in the preceding sentence shall be deemed to be original signatures for all purposes.

9.05.(3).sec=	Notwithstanding the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act (15 U.S.C. section 7001 et seq.) or any other Legal Requirement relating to or enabling the creation, execution, delivery, or recordation of any contract or signature by electronic means, and notwithstanding any course of conduct engaged in by the Parties, no Party shall be deemed to have executed this Agreement or any other document contemplated by this Agreement (including any amendment or other change thereto) unless and until such Party shall have executed this Agreement or such document on paper by a handwritten original signature or any other symbol executed or adopted by a Party with current intention to authenticate this Agreement or such other contemplated document and an original of such signature has been exchanged by the Parties either by physical delivery or in the manner set forth in Section 9.05(b). "Originally signed” or "original signature” means or refers to a signature that has not been mechanically or electronically reproduced.

9.06.Ti=	Governing Law.  

This Agreement and the agreements, instruments and documents contemplated hereby, shall be governed by, and construed in accordance with, the Legal Requirements of the State of Delaware, without regard to any applicable principles of conflicts of law that might require the application of the Legal Requirements of any other jurisdiction.

9.07.Ti=	Exclusive Jurisdiction; Venue.  

In any action or proceeding between any of the Parties arising out of or relating to this Agreement or any of the Contemplated Transactions, each of the Parties: (a) irrevocably and unconditionally consents and submits to the exclusive jurisdiction and venue of the Court of Chancery of the State of Delaware or to the extent such court does not have subject matter jurisdiction, the Superior Court of the State of Delaware or the United States District Court for the District of Delaware, (b) agrees that all claims in respect of such action or proceeding shall be heard and determined exclusively in accordance with clause (a) of this Section, (c) waives any objection to laying venue in any such action or proceeding in such courts, (d) waives any objection that such courts are an inconvenient forum or do not have jurisdiction over any party, and (e) agrees that service of process upon such party in any such action or proceeding shall be effective if given in accordance with Section 9.12 of this Agreement.

9.08.Ti=	Waiver of Jury Trial.  

Each of the parties irrevocably waives any and all rights to trial by jury in any action or proceeding between the Parties arising out of or relating to this Agreement and the Contemplated Transactions.

9.09.Ti=	Disclosure Schedules.  

The Company Disclosure Schedule and the Parent Disclosure Schedule shall be arranged in separate Parts corresponding to the numbered and lettered sections contained in Article III and Article IV, respectively.  The information disclosed in any numbered or lettered Part shall be deemed to relate to and to qualify the particular representation or warranty set forth in the corresponding numbered or lettered section in Article III or Article IV, as the case may be, and each other representation or warranty to the extent that such information is relevant to such other section or subsection.

9.10.Ti=	Assignments and Successors.  

No Party may assign any of its rights or delegate any of its obligations under this Agreement without the prior written consent of the other Parties.  Any attempted assignment of this Agreement or of any such rights or delegation of obligations without such consent shall be void and of no effect  This Agreement will be binding upon, and shall be enforceable by and inure solely to the benefit of, the parties hereto and their respective successors and permitted assigns and the third party beneficiaries identified in Section 9.12.

9.11.Ti=	No Third Party Rights.  

Nothing in this Agreement, express or implied, is intended to or shall confer upon any Person (other than the Parties) any right, benefit or remedy of any nature whatsoever under or by reason of this Agreement; provided, that after the Effective Time, (a) the Indemnified Persons shall be third party beneficiaries of, and entitled to enforce, Section 6.14 and (b) following the Effective Time, the provisions of Article II relating to the payment of the [Merger Consideration and Award Amounts] shall be enforceable by the holders of Common Stock or [Company Awards] immediately prior to the Effective Time. 9.13.(1).(5).sec=	reference to any Legal Requirement means such Legal Requirement as amended, modified, codified, replaced or reenacted, in whole or in part, and in effect from time to time, including rules and regulations promulgated thereunder, and reference to any section or other provision of any Legal Requirement means that provision of such Legal Requirement from time to time in effect and constituting the substantive amendment, modification, codification, replacement or reenactment of such section or other provision;

This Agreement was negotiated by the Parties with the benefit of legal representation and any rule of construction or interpretation otherwise requiring this Agreement to be construed or interpreted against any Party shall not apply to any construction or interpretation hereof.

9.13.(3).sec=	Headings.  The headings contained in this Agreement are for convenience of reference only, shall not be deemed to be a part of this Agreement and shall not be referred to in connection with the construction or interpretation of this Agreement.

9.14.Ti=	Enforcement of Agreement.  

The Parties acknowledge and agree that the Company would be irreparably damaged if any of the provisions of this Agreement are not performed in accordance with their specific terms and that any breach of this Agreement by the Parent of Purchaser could not be adequately compensated by monetary damages alone.  Accordingly, in addition to any other right or remedy to which Company may be entitled, at law or in equity, it shall be entitled, without proof of damages, to enforce any provision of this Agreement by a decree of specific performance and temporary, preliminary and permanent injunctive relief to prevent breaches or threatened breaches of any of the provisions of this Agreement, without posting any bond or other undertaking.  In the event that any action shall be brought by Company in equity to enforce the provisions of the Agreement, neither Parent nor Purchaser shall allege, and each hereby waives the defense, that there is an adequate remedy at law or that the award of specific performance is not an appropriate remedy for any reason of law or equity.

9.15.Ti=	Severability.  

If any provision of this Agreement is held invalid, illegal or unenforceable by any court of competent jurisdiction, the other provisions of this Agreement will remain in full force and effect, so long as the economic or legal substance of the transactions contemplated by this Agreement is not affected in any manner materially adverse to any Party.

9.16.Ti=	Certain Definitions:  

"Acceptance Time” means the acceptance for payment of any shares of the Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer.

COMMENT:

Section 251(h) is designed to minimize the delay between closing of the front-end tender offer and the back-end merger.  If the front-end tender offer and the back-end merger can close virtually simultaneously then, among other things, the bidder may be able to utilize the assets of the target as collateral for its debt financing.

In order to effect a Section 251(h) merger, the front-end tender offer must be "consummated.”  Although Section 801.33 of the HSR Act contains a definition of "consummation” ("the acceptance for payment of any shares tendered in a tender offer”), neither the SEC nor the DGCL contains such a definition.  

Because the concept of "Acceptance Time” may be viewed as a proxy for the term "consummate,” parties may consider defining Acceptance Time as the "acceptance of payment” without referring to the "payment by Purchaser for” shares, as is reflected in the language above.

However, particularly in a non-Section 251(h) transaction, "Acceptance Time” may be defined as the time when Purchaser accepts for payment and pays for the tendered shares.  Under this definition, Purchaser and Parent would not become entitled to designate directors under Section 1.04 until after Purchaser actually pays for the tendered shares on the theory that it is not until that time that Purchaser actually achieves ownership of such shares and becomes entitled to the corresponding rights of a stockholder.  [NTD:  Add commentary as to whether purchaser would propose standard of acceptance, without regard to actual payment.]

"Acquiring Person” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.22.

"Acquisition Proposal” means any offer, proposal, inquiry or indication of interest (other than an offer, proposal, inquiry or indication of interest by Parent or Purchaser) contemplating or otherwise relating to any Acquisition Transaction.

"Acquisition Transaction” means any transaction or series of transactions involving:

(a)	any merger, consolidation, share exchange, business combination, issuance of securities, acquisition of securities, tender offer, exchange offer or other similar transaction (i) in which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is a constituent corporation, (ii) in which a Person or "group” (as defined in the Exchange Act and the rules promulgated thereunder) of Persons directly or indirectly acquires beneficial or record ownership of securities representing more than 20% of the outstanding securities of any class of voting securities of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries, or (iii) in which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries issues or sells securities representing more than 20% of the outstanding securities of any class of voting securities of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries; or

(b)	any sale (other than sales of inventory in the ordinary course of business), lease (other than in the ordinary course of business), exchange, transfer (other than sales of inventory in the ordinary course of business), license (other than nonexclusive licenses in the ordinary course of business), acquisition or disposition of any business or businesses or assets that constitute or account for 20% or more of the consolidated net revenues, net income or assets of the Company and its Subsidiaries.

"Affiliate” means, with respect to any Person, another Person that directly or indirectly, through one or more intermediaries, controls, is controlled by, or is under common control with, such first Person.

"Agreement” shall have the meaning set forth in the Preamble.

["Antitrust Laws” means the HSR Act and any other antitrust, unfair competition, merger or acquisition notification, or merger or acquisition control Legal Requirements under any applicable jurisdictions, whether federal, state, local or foreign.]

"Applicable Date” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.04(a).

"Appraisal Shares” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 2.07.

"Blue Sky Laws” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.02(c).

"Board Recommendation” means the recommendation of the Company Board that the holders of the Company Common Stock accept the Offer and tender their shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer.

COMMENT:

Because this Model Agreement is governed by Section 251(h) and no stockholder vote to approve the back-end merger is necessary, the Board Recommendation relates only to tendering shares into the Offer.  If Section 251(h) were inapplicable, consider defined Board Recommendation to mean "the recommendation of the Company Board that the holders of the Company Common Stock accept the Offer and tender their shares of Company Common Stock pursuant to the Offer and to vote to approve and adopt this Agreement and the Merger at the Company Stockholders’ Meeting.”

"Book Entry Shares” mean uncertificated shares of Company Common Stock represented by a book entry.

"business day” means any day other than a Saturday, Sunday or a day on which banking institutions located in [City, State] are authorized pursuant to Legal Requirement to be closed and shall consist of the time period from 12:01 a.m. through 12:00 midnight at such location.

"Certificate of Merger” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 2.02.

"Certificates” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 2.06(b).

"CFR” means the United States Code of Federal Regulations.

"Change in Recommendation” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 5.02(c).

"Claim” has the meaning set forth in Section 6.16(b).

"Closing” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 2.02.

"Closing Agreement” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.10(k).

"Closing Date” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 2.02.

"Company” shall have the meaning set forth in the Preamble.

"Company Balance Sheet” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.05(a).

"Company Benefit Plans” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.11(b)(i).

"Company Board” means the board of directors of the Company.

"Company Common Stock” shall have the meaning set forth in the Preamble.

["Company Contract” means any Contract: (a) to which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is a party; (b) by which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries or any asset of the Company or any of its Subsidiaries is or may become bound or under which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries has, or may become subject to, any obligation; or (c) under which the Company or any of its Subsidiaries has or may acquire any right or interest.]

"Company Compensation Agreement” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.11(v).

["Company Disclosure Schedule” means the disclosure schedule that has been prepared by the Company in accordance with the requirements of [Section 9.10] and that has been delivered by the Company to Parent on the date of this Agreement and signed by the President of the Company.]

"Company Employees” has the meaning set forth in Section 6.11.

"Company Equity Awards” means awards of Company Stock Options, Company Restricted Stock and Company RSUs.

"Company IP” means all Intellectual Property owned, used, held for use or exploited by the Company or any of the Company Subsidiaries, including all Owned Company IP and Licensed Company IP.

["Company Material Adverse Effect” means events, violations, circumstances or other matters which, individually or in the aggregate, had or could reasonably be expected to have a material adverse effect on (i) the business, condition, capitalization, assets, liabilities, operations, financial performance or prospects of the Company and its Subsidiaries taken as a whole, (ii) the ability of the Company to consummate the Merger or any of the other Contemplated Transactions or to perform any of its obligations under the Agreement, or (iii) Parent’s ability to vote, receive dividends with respect to or otherwise exercise ownership rights with respect to the stock of the Surviving Corporation.]

["Company Stockholders’ Meeting” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 6.04(b).]

"Controlled Group Liability” shall have the meaning set forth in Section 3.11(a).

"Copyrights” means all copyrights, copyrightable works, semiconductor topography and mask work rights, and applications for registration thereof, including all rights of authorship, use, publication, reproduction, distribution, performance transformation, moral rights and rights of ownership of copyrightable works, semiconductor topography works and mask works, and all rights to register and obtain renewals and extensions of registrations, together with all other interests accruing by reason of international copyright, semiconductor topography and mask work conventions.
