ANNEX A

CONDITIONS OF THE OFFER

Capitalized terms used but not defined herein shall have the meanings ascribed to them in the Agreement.  Notwithstanding any other term of the Offer or the Agreement, Purchaser shall not be required to, and Parent shall not be required to cause Purchaser to, accept for payment or, subject to any applicable rules and regulations of the SEC, including Rule 14e-1(c) under the Exchange Act, pay for any shares of the Company Common Stock tendered pursuant to the Offer, and, to the extent permitted by this Agreement, may amend or terminate the Offer, unless, at the time of expiration of the Offer:

COMMENT:

Rule 14e-1(c) under the Exchange Act, as referenced in the preamble to the conditions, requires Purchaser to pay for or return tendered shares of the Company Common Stock promptly after the termination or withdrawal of the Offer.

It is important to include a statement in the preamble to the conditions of the offer on the timing of the satisfaction of the conditions.  Specifying that the conditions must be satisfied at the time of the expiration of the Offer assures the Purchaser that all the conditions to the Offer are satisfied before there is an obligation to purchase the Shares of Company Common Stock.  If such a statement is not included, the Purchaser could be in the position of having to purchase the Company Common Stock if the conditions were satisfied at any time prior to the expiration of the Offer, even if they were no longer satisfied at such time.

(i)	there shall have been validly tendered and not withdrawn prior to the expiration of the Offer that number of shares of the Company Common Stock that, together with shares of the Company Common Stock already owned by Purchaser, would represent at least a majority of the outstanding Company Common Stock (the "Minimum Tender Condition”) (for purposes of determining whether the Minimum Tender Condition has been satisfied, Company Common Stock tendered in the Offer pursuant to guaranteed delivery procedures that have not yet been delivered in settlement or satisfaction of such guarantee shall not be considered validly tendered and not withdrawn), and    

COMMENT:

Minimum Tender Condition.  Section 251(h) requires that, following consummation of the Offer, Purchaser "own” at least that percentage of shares as would be required to vote to adopt the Merger Agreement if Section 251(h) were inapplicable.  By statute, that vote requirement is a majority of the outstanding shares entitled to vote on the merger.  However, a company’s charter may include a higher vote threshold.

In non-Section 251(h) deals, in determining the number of shares that must be tendered to satisfy the Minimum Tender Condition, the parties should consider whether to use a denominator based on either:

(i)	the shares actually outstanding, or

(ii)	the fully diluted, or some variation of the diluted, shares outstanding (that is, reflecting the potential for shares that may be issued to options and other derivative or contingent rights).

Using the outstanding amount would decrease the number of shares required to satisfy the Minimum Tender Condition and therefore make it more likely that the Minimum Tender Condition would be met.  However, closing on just a majority of the outstanding shares might expose a purchaser to the risk that prior to the vote on the back-end merger or the time of determination of whether the purchaser holds enough shares to allow the purchaser to effect a short-form merger, more Company shares might be issued, such as pursuant to outstanding options, so that the purchaser no longer holds a majority of the outstanding shares.  [NTD:  Note why not this is not an issue in 251(h) deals.]

While the most common threshold has been the fully-diluted shares number, variations exist, such as counting only those derivative securities that are likely to be vested at the time of the shareholder meeting or short-form merger, or counting only those securities that are "in the money” based on the Offer price.

If a fully diluted concept is used, one potential definition is as follows:  

"The term "Fully Diluted Shares” means all outstanding securities entitled generally to vote in the election of directors of the Company on a fully diluted basis, after giving effect to the exercise or conversion of all Options, rights and securities convertible or exercisable into such voting securities on or prior to the Closing Date (other than the Top-Up Option).”  

This definition limits the time parameters to include only those shares that could in fact be issued upon conversion or exercise during the relevant time frame.  Alternatively, the definition could instead include all shares issuable upon conversion or exercise, regardless of the conversion or exercise price, the vesting schedule or other terms and conditions thereof.

Requirement of Purchaser Ownership.  Another consideration is that under each of Section 251(h), Section 253 and Section 267 of the DGCL, Purchaser must "own” 90% of the Company’s shares.  The DGCL generally defines "ownership” as record ownership.  Accordingly, purchasers generally coordinate in advance with the Company’s transfer agent to transfer ownership of the shares to Purchaser on the transfer agent’s records in connection with the closing of the tender offer.  Also for this reason, Parent should transfer to Purchaser any shares of the Company it may own.  Finally, shares delivered by notice of guaranteed delivery should be excluded.

(ii)	any waiting period applicable to the transactions contemplated by the Agreement (including the Offer and the Merger) under the HSR Act shall have expired or been terminated.

COMMENT:  

The proposed merger, unless an exception is available under the HSR Act, will require the submission of a HSR filing if the relevant thresholds are satisfied.  Both Purchaser and the Company are required to make separate filings.  Once the filings are made, the waiting period begins.  The waiting period is normally 30 days but is 16 days for cash tender offers.  For additional discussion regarding the HSR Act, see the commentary to Article 4 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement.

Furthermore, notwithstanding any other term of the Offer or this Agreement, Purchaser shall not be required to, and Parent shall not be required to cause Purchaser to, accept for payment or, subject as aforesaid, to pay for any shares of the Company Common Stock not theretofore accepted for payment or paid for if, at any time on or after the date of this Agreement and before the expiration of the Offer, any of the following conditions exists and is continuing at the expiration of the Offer:

(a)	any Order or other Law preventing the consummation of the Merger issued or promulgated by any Governmental Body of competent jurisdiction (a "Government Action”) shall be in effect, provided, that Parent and Purchaser have used commercially reasonable efforts to oppose any such Government Action;

(b)	the representations and warranties of the Company (i) contained in Section 3.11(u) shall not be true and correct in all respects as of the expiration of the Offer as if made at and as of such date, and (ii) contained in the Agreement, other than Section 3.11(u), shall not be true and correct as of the expiration of the Offer as if made at and as of such date (except to the extent that any such representations and warranties speak as of a specified date, in which case only as of such specified date) and the failure or failures of such representations and warranties to be so true and correct has had a Company Material Adverse Effect; 

(c)	the Company shall have failed to perform in all respects its agreements and covenants to be performed or complied with by it contained in Section 6.10 and shall not have cured such breach, failure to perform or noncompliance; 

COMMENT: 

Sections (b) and (c) treat the representations and covenants regarding Rule 14d-10 matters differently than the other representations, warranties and covenants contained in the Agreement.  The Rule 14d-10 matters can be considered to be "fundamental” representations and covenants in the tender offer context.  As more fully discussed in the comments to Sections 3.11 and 6.10 above, the Rule 14d-10 references to the best price rule and the safe harbor for certain compensatory agreements are critical to the Offer [and thus are not appropriately subject to a materiality qualifier].  [NTD:  Is this always the case?]  For a more complete discussion of fundamental representations, see Comments to Section 5.1.  As this is a Seller’s first draft, the tolerance level on the bringdown of the representations and warranties is fairly high.  A more buyer-friendly formulation which strips the materiality qualifiers for purposes of the bringdown would be as follows:

"(b) the representations and warranties of the Company (i) contained in Section 3.11(u) shall not be true and correct in all respects as of the expiration of the Offer as if made at and as of such date, and (ii) contained in the Agreement, other than Section 3.11(u), shall not be true and correct (without giving effect to any limitation as to "materiality” or any derivative thereof or "Company Material Adverse Effect” set forth therein) as of the expiration of the Offer as if made at and as of such date (except to the extent that any such representations and warranties speak as of a specified date, in which case only as of such specified date) and the failure or failures of such representations and warranties to be so true and correct (without giving effect to any limitation as to "materiality” or any derivative thereof or "Company Material Adverse Effect” set forth therein) has had a Company Material Adverse Effect; 

(c)	the Company (i) shall have failed to perform in all respects its agreements and covenants to be performed or complied with by it contained in Section 6.10 and shall not have cured such breach, failure to perform or noncompliance, and (ii) shall have failed to perform in all material respects its agreements and covenants to be performed or complied with by it under this Agreement, other than as described in clause (i) above, and shall not have cured such breach, failure to perform or noncompliance;”

The relative importance of the representations and warranties and the trigger thresholds are deal specific and are subject to extensive negotiation.

(d)	this Agreement shall have been terminated in accordance with its terms; or

(e)	the occurrence of any Company Material Adverse Effect.

The foregoing conditions may be waived by Purchaser and Parent in whole or in part at any time and from time to time in their sole discretion (other than the Minimum Tender Condition).  The failure by Parent or Purchaser at any time to exercise any of the foregoing rights shall not be deemed a waiver of any such right, the waiver of any such right with respect to particular facts and circumstances shall not be deemed a waiver with respect to any other facts and circumstances and each such right shall be deemed an ongoing right that may be asserted at any time and from time to time.

COMMENT:

The conditions to the Offer are events that must occur or circumstances that must exist before Parent is obligated to accept any shares of the Company Common Stock tendered pursuant to the Offer.  If any of the conditions in Annex A are not satisfied, then Parent may decline to proceed with the Offer and the Merger until the conditions are satisfied and, under certain circumstances, may terminate the Agreement in accordance with Article VIII.

Purchasers may attempt to make their obligation to close an Offer subject to as many conditions as possible and will negotiate a variety of conditions that provide them with an opportunity to decline to complete the Offer.  Conversely, targets generally desire to limit the conditions to a Purchaser’s obligation to close.  A target wants to assure that the transaction is closed as negotiated, and further is concerned that announcement of the transaction has the potential to affect adversely the target’s business and constituents.  Failure to close or even uncertainty as to closing may disrupt the target’s relationships with its executives, employees, suppliers, customers and stockholders.  Such disruption could leave the target weaker than it was before the transaction was announced.  Targets also strive to minimize a Purchaser’s closing conditions because, if Purchaser refuses to consummate the transaction on the basis that a closing condition is not fulfilled, the target may be viewed as "damaged goods” and this may negatively affect its ability to merge with another buyer or its ability to obtain a fair price in another merger.  Purchasers may also be concerned with deal protection, particularly if the transaction is strategic or transformational to Purchaser.

Scope and Waiver of Conditions of the Offer.  The conditions of the offer vary from deal to deal and there is no "correct” set of closing conditions.  However, the conditions that may be used for a tender offer are limited in comparison to the conditions that may be used for the closing of a merger or stock purchase.  In the non-tender offer situation, the parties generally negotiate conditions to closing without regulatory intervention, allowing the parties to set any conditions they deem desirable.  In the tender offer context, however, the SEC may limit the conditions that can be used. 

The SEC provides some guidance regarding the scope of any conditions to a tender offer.  

•	A tender offer may be conditioned on a variety of events and circumstances, provided that they are not within the direct or indirect control of the bidder.  

•	The conditions must be drafted with sufficient specificity to allow for an objective verification of whether or not the conditions have been satisfied.  If there are conditions in a tender offer where the determination of whether or not a condition has been triggered is in the sole judgment of the bidder, such a condition may render the Offer to be considered "illusory,” that is, providing the bidder a right to refuse to consummate the offer at its own discretion.  In addition, the SEC has advised that broadly drafted conditions can make it impossible for a security holder to determine what events or occurrences will allow the bidder to terminate the offer.  

•	Conditions that may be triggered at any time and for any reason also may cause the offer to be considered illusory.  For example, the SEC commented unfavorably upon a tender offer condition that stated that there shall not have occurred "the commencement or escalation of a war, armed hostilities or other international or national crisis directly or indirectly involving the United States,” cautioning that the cited language lacked specificity in the type of international crises that would trigger the condition.  

•	The SEC has determined that illusory offers contravene the prohibitions against fraudulent, deceptive or manipulative acts or practices within the meaning of Section 14(e) of the Exchange Act.  See In re Pabst Brewing Co. & APL Corp., CCH Blue Sky L. Rep. ¶ 71,415 (Wis. Comm’r Sec. 1978).  

The Agreement does not provide an exhaustive list of all possible closing conditions, but does include closing conditions that are frequently seen in offers of this type.  Some additional conditions that may merit consideration for inclusion in the Agreement are as follows:

•	Financing.  Purchaser has been unable, prior to the expiration of the Offer, to obtain financing [pursuant to the terms and conditions contained in the Commitment Letter and otherwise] reasonably satisfactory to Purchaser that will be sufficient for Purchaser to acquire all of the Shares tendered pursuant to the Offer[ and pay related fees and expenses].

•	Suspension of Trading.  There shall have occurred (i) any general suspension of trading in, or limitation on prices for, securities on any national securities exchange of in the over-the-counter market in the United States, (ii) a declaration of a banking moratorium or any suspension of payments in respect of banks in the United States (whether or not mandatory), or (iii)  any significant adverse change in the market price of the Company Common Stock or in the securities or financial markets of the United States.

•	No Other Tender Offers.  (a) A tender or exchange offer for some or all of the shares of Company Common Stock has been publicly proposed to be made or has been made by another person (including the Company or any of its subsidiaries or affiliates), or has been publicly disclosed, or (b) any person or group has entered into a definitive agreement or an agreement in principle or made a proposal with respect to a tender or exchange offer or a merger, consolidation or other business combination with or involving the Company.

•	[SEC Approval.  The SEC has not confirmed to Purchaser and Company that it has completed its review of, and has no further comments on, the Schedule TO and related Schedule 14D-9.]  [NTD:  How common is this in the tender offer context?]

Parent may elect to pay for any shares of the Company Common Stock tendered pursuant to the Offer despite the non-fulfillment of a Condition of the Offer.  Parties often agree that their closing conditions may only be waived in writing to avoid disputes about whether a party has actually waived a closing condition.  See Comment to Section 8.2(b).

For additional discussion regarding the application and drafting of each of these conditions, see Article 5 of the ABA Model Merger Agreement.

Waiver of Conditions.  The Agreement provides that the conditions can be waived at any time by Purchaser and that the failure to exercise any rights in the conditions shall not be deemed to be a waiver of these rights.  However, the SEC has taken the position that if a condition is triggered and Purchaser proceeds with Offer, Purchaser has waived the condition.  As such, Purchaser should bear in mind that any waiver of a condition must be communicated and confirmed formally and not through its conduct.  Thus, depending on the materiality of the condition and the time until expiration of the Offer, Purchaser may need to extend the Offer and circulate revised tender offer materials to security holders.

Financing Condition.  [A Purchaser’s Offer extension often relates to the financing condition.]  The SEC has articulated the position that a material change in the Offer occurs when the financing condition is satisfied.  Thus the SEC would require that the Offer should remain open for at least five days following satisfaction.  This requirement can prove problematic as the definitive terms for the financing often are not finalized until the last moment.  In that particular case, the Offer period would need to be extended.  In the case of a firm, legally binding commitment for financing, Purchaser could argue that the financing condition is not a "true” financing condition and thus may be able to avoid the extension of the Offer. 

ANNEX B

CERTIFICATE OF INCORPORATION



OF



[SURVIVING CORPORATION]

ARTICLE I

The name of the corporation (the "Corporation”) is [_____________].

ARTICLE II

The address of the Corporation’s registered office in the State of Delaware is in New Castle County, at ________________________.  The name of the registered agent at such address is The Corporation Service Company.

ARTICLE III

The purpose of the Corporation is to engage in any lawful act or activity for which corporations may be organized under the General Corporation Law of the State of Delaware.

ARTICLE IV

The total number of shares of all classes of stock that the Corporation shall have authority to issue is 1,000 shares of Common Stock having the par value of $0.01 per share.

ARTICLE V

The number of directors of the Corporation shall be fixed from time to time by the Board of Directors of the Corporation.

ARTICLE VI

In furtherance and not in limitation of the powers conferred upon it by law, the Board of Directors of the Corporation is expressly authorized to adopt, amend or repeal the Bylaws of the Corporation.

ARTICLE VII

Unless and except to the extent that the Bylaws of the Corporation so require, the election of directors of the Corporation need not be by written ballot.

ARTICLE VIII

To the fullest extent from time to time permitted by law, no director of the Corporation shall be personally liable to any extent to the Corporation or its stockholders for monetary damages for breach of his fiduciary duty as a director.

ARTICLE IX

Each person who is or was or had agreed to become a director or officer of the Corporation, and each such person who is or was serving or who had agreed to serve at the request of the Corporation as a director, officer, partner, member, employee or agent of another corporation, partnership, limited liability company, joint venture, trust or other enterprise (including the heirs, executor, administrators or estate of such person), shall be indemnified and advanced expenses by the Corporation to the fullest extent permitted from time to time by applicable law.
